5.
City Council 2026 Regular Meeting Calendar — Adoption
Adopt the City Council Regular Meeting schedule for the calendar year 2026 and, pursuant to Charter Section
2.10, authorize relocating the January 12 and January 26, 2026, Regular City Council Meetings to the Main
Library.
CEQA: This action is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an organizational or administrative activity that
will not result in direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(5).)
6.
Participation in National Opioid Settlement Agreement — Approval
Approve the City’s participation in a no-cost opioid settlement agreement with Mylan and authorize the City
Attorney to execute documents confirming the City’s participation and electing to have the settlement funds be
provided directly to the City of San Mateo.
CEQA: This proposed action is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an organizational or administrative
activity that will not result in direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section
15378(b)(5).)
7.
Sycamore Tree Pruning – Agreement
Approve an agreement with West Coast Tree Service, Inc. for sycamore tree pruning in the amount of $120,756;
authorize a 10% contingency of $12,075, for a total amount not to exceed $132,831; and authorize the Director
of Parks and Recreation to execute the agreement in substantially the form presented and issue change orders
within the contingency amount.
CEQA: This Project is categorically exempt from CEQA as an “existing facility,” because it consists of the operation,
repair, maintenance, permitting, leasing, licensing, or minor alteration of existing public or private structures,
facilities, mechanical equipment, or topographical features, involving negligible or no expansion of use. (CEQA
Guidelines Section 15301.)
8.
Public Works Facilities Program Manager – Professional Services Agreement
Approve an agreement with ArcPath Project Delivery, Inc. to provide professional program management services
to the Public Works Facilities division from Fiscal Year 2025-26 through Fiscal Year 2027-28 in the amount of
$300,000; and authorize the Public Works Director to execute the agreement in substantially the form presented
and issue amendments within the agreement amount.
CEQA: This project is categorically exempt from CEQA as an “existing facility,” because it consists of the operation,
repair, maintenance, permitting, leasing, licensing, or minor alteration of existing public or private structures,
facilities, mechanical equipment, or topographical features, involving negligible or no expansion of existing or
former use. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15301.)
9.
Wastewater Treatment Plant Upgrade and Expansion Project – Approval
Approve an increase to the contingency reserve to the construction agreement with Sundt Construction, Inc. for
the Wastewater Treatment Plant Nutrient Removal and Wet Weather Flow Management Upgrade and Expansion
Project in the amount of $773,702, for a total contingency amount of $61,193,702; and authorize the Public
Works Director to issue change orders within the contingency amount.
CEQA: The City prepared a Final Programmatic Environmental Impact Report (Final PEIR) in accordance with the
California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA) (SCH No. 2015032006). Council on June 6, 2016, certified the PEIR. In
accordance with CEQA, the Final PEIR serves as the primary environmental compliance document for the
implementation of the Clean Water Program. The City prepared Addenda to the Final PEIR that was approved on
July 16, 2018 (Addendum 1) and April 15, 2019 (Addendum 2). This work is within the scope of the Project

11.
Peninsula Corridor Multimodal Complete Streets Project — Grant Application
Adopt a Resolution approving the submittal of a grant application for $1,125,000, with a local match in the
amount of $245,000, to the San Mateo County Transportation Authority (SMCTA) for Highway Program Grant
Funding for the Peninsula Avenue Multi-Modal Corridor Study; and authorize the City Manager to take any other
actions necessary to receive grant funds including executing a supplemental agreement or amendment to the
Primary Grant Agreement with the SMCTA and the City of Burlingame relating to funding for the project.
CEQA: Adoption of this Resolution approving a grant application to the San Mateo County Transportation
Authority is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is a government fiscal activity which does not involve any
commitment to any specific project which may result in a potentially significant impact on the environment.
(CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(4).)

CEQA: This Project is categorically exempt from CEQA as an “existing facility,” because it consists of the operation,

former use. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15301.)

Adopt a Resolution to approve Amendment No. 3 to the agreement with DTSM Housing LLC for exclusive

PUBLIC COMMENT
Members of the public wishing to comment on any item not appearing on the agenda may address the City Council at this time. State
law prevents Council from taking action on any matter not on the agenda; your comments may be referred to staff for follow up.
Public comment is limited to a total of 15 minutes; however, an opportunity for additional public comment may be provided later in
the agenda.
 
NEW BUSINESS
16.
Animal Control Amendments — Ordinance Introduction
Introduce an Ordinance amending San Mateo Municipal Code Chapter 8.02 "Animal Control" and adding Chapter
8.34 “Animal Fanciers Permit” to maintain enforceability and alignment with San Mateo County's Animal Control
Ordinance.
CEQA: This action is not a project subject to CEQA, because it can be seen with certainty that it will not cause a
physical change in the environment. (Public Resources Code Section 21065.)
OLD BUSINESS
17.
Gas Leaf Blower Prohibition — Update
Provide direction on how to update the leaf blower Ordinance to prohibit the use of gas leaf blowers.
CEQA: This Council action in receiving an informational update and providing feedback for the development of an
Ordinance prohibiting gas leaf blowers and additional leaf blower regulations is not a “project” subject to CEQA
review, in that it consists of the planning for possible future actions which the City has not approved, adopted, or
funded. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15262.)
REPORTS AND ANNOUNCEMENTS
City Manager, City Attorney and Council Members report on their various assignments and liaison roles and Council requests for
scheduling future items.
 
ADJOURNMENT

WATCHING A MEETING ON TV: City Council meetings are broadcast live on Comcast/channel 27, Wave/channel 26, or AT&T/channel 99.
For transmission problems during the broadcast, please call (650) 522-7099. For all other broadcast comments, call (650) 522-7040, Monday-Friday,

1) Public Meeting Portal www.cityofsanmateo.org/publicmeetings
2) City YouTube channel and stream it on YouTube: http://youtube.com/CityofSanMateo
3) Watch TV live stream: https://www.cityofsanmateo.org/193/Channel-San-Mateo-Live-Stream 
PUBLIC COMMENTS/REQUEST TO SPEAK
Prior to the Meeting 
Send comments to: clerk@cityofsanmateo.org until 4 p.m. the day of the meeting.
During the meeting
By Zoom: Click the link at the top of the agenda and you’ll be added to the meeting. All attendees are muted by default. When the item of interest
is open for consideration, select the “Raise Your Hand” icon and you will be called on at the appropriate time.
By telephone: Call (408) 638-0968 and enter the conference ID found at the top of the meeting agenda. When the item of interest is open for
consideration, select *9 to raise your hand. When called upon, press *6 to unmute, state your name and provide your comments.
In Person: At the meeting complete a “Request to Speak” form. Organized Group and Presentations: Up to five (5) minutes for a group presentation,
with as many speakers as can be accommodated within that time allowance. To qualify for a group presentation, all individuals associated with the
presentation must be clearly identified and confirmed as in attendance at the meeting. Presentation materials must be submitted to
clerk@cityofsanmateo.org one (1) business day in advance of the meeting.
ACCESSIBILITY: In compliance with the Americans with Disabilities Act and to ensure meaningful access for all participants, including those with
limited English proficiency, individuals requiring special accommodations or language assistance to participate in this meeting may contact the City
Clerk’s Office at (650) 522-7040 or clerk@cityofsanmateo.org . Notification 48 hours prior to the meeting will enable the City to make reasonable
arrangements to ensure accessibility to this meeting.

330 W. 20th Avenue

www.cityofsanmateo.org
 
September 15, 2025
City Hall Council Chambers 5:30 PM
Special Meeting
 
CALL TO ORDER at 5:30 p.m.
Roll Call
Present: Mayor Newsom, Deputy Mayor Loraine, Council Members: Fernandez, Diaz Nash and Cwirko-Godycki
AB 2449 Requests and Considerations for Meeting Participation by Teleconference due to Just Cause or Emergency 
Circumstances – there were no requests. 
CLOSED SESSION
Councilmember Fernandez recused herself from Item 1 as her employer is another party to the litigation matter at issue.
Following the opportunity for public comment, there were no speakers, the City Council convened into Closed Session at 
5:32 p.m. to consider:
1.
Conference with Legal Counsel — Existing Litigation
(Paragraph (1) of subdivision (d) of Section 54956.9)
Name of case: Neville v. City of San Mateo et al. (San Mateo Superior Court Case No. 25-CIV-05067)
City Council reconvened from Closed Session at 5:42 p.m. to consider:
STUDY SESSION
2.
Street Vending: Current Regulations, Enforcement Challenges, and Policy Options – Presentation
Eugene Alper, Code Enforcement Manager and Kristen Aiu, Sr. Code Enforcement Officer gave the presentation.
Public Comment: Dianne Whitaker noted increase use of the artificial turf sports field at Martin Luther King Park 
and food vendors on-site, with concerns about traffic safety and possible regulatory violations. Kevin Simpson 
expressed the disruptions caused by food trucks in residential areas and calls for action to address safety and 
noise issues.
Council asked questions and made comments. Council directed staff to explore options to enhance enforcement 
using existing rules and regulations (Option 2), including enhancing the enforcement of the 72-hour parking rule 
by Parking Enforcement, investigating ways to improve compliance with business tax certificate (license) 
requirements, and strengthening collaboration and communication with County Health regarding food vendor 
permits. Additionally, Council directed staff to explore language to include in the upcoming development of the 
state legislative platform that would support greater ability for cities to enforce their own food vending 
ordinance (Option 4). Staff will provide periodic updates to the Council on the implementation of their direction.
ADJOURNMENT –The meeting adjourned at 7:10 p.m.

9.
19th Avenue / Fashion Island Boulevard Multimodal Improvement Project — Informational Update
Bethany Lopez, Senior Engineer, gave the presentation.
Public Comment: 
Kevin Simpson supported the project for improving safety and clarity for both drivers and cyclists, 
and emphasized its importance for school access and family mobility. Brendan Tsih shared biking 
experiences and concerns about safety for young cyclists. Tom Tsih voiced general support for the 
project goals and emphasized the importance of continued community input. Andrew Uto-Uko 
supported safer bike infrastructure based on personal experience biking to school. Rick Sakuoa 
expressed support for safety but raised concerns about certain project elements and emphasized the 
need for thorough review and collaboration. Taso Zografos highlighted the need for data-informed 
planning and raised questions about priorities within the project. Maya Molc supported the design 
and offered ideas to improve visibility and safety for cyclists. Henry Adams shared experiences biking 
with his children and supported clearer separation between bike and car traffic. Kevin Milhoan 
shared safety concerns from commuting by bike and expressed strong support for improvements to 
current infrastructure. Michael Ragan emphasized the need to listen to residents and consider 
community input carefully due to the scale and complexity of the project. Rich Hedges supported the 
project overall, especially safety and traffic improvements, and encouraged consideration of key 
design adjustments. Sema Patel spoke in strong support of the project, citing safety data, funding 
value, and future development in the area. Susan Manheimer expressed concerns about traffic 
impacts and emergency access. and requested further review of potential congestion issues. Annie 
Tsai supported the project based on personal experience and community needs, emphasizing safety 
and access for all users. Anna Lieb expressed general support for the project and the focus on safety. 
Marvette Uto-Uko Supported the project and shared a question related to bike safety. Mike Swire 
spoke in favor of the project and offered a few concerns and suggestions.
crosswalks.
Council asked questions and made comments. Council offered feedback regarding bike network gaps, 
parking changes, and congestion surrounding the project area.
Council recessed from 10:13 p.m. to 10:18 p.m.
PUBLIC HEARING

REPORTS AND ANNOUNCEMENTS
City Manager, City Attorney and Council Members report on their various assignments and liaison roles and Council 
requests for scheduling future items. 
Council received confirmation that the speed survey work is underway and scheduled to continue over the next 
eight months, with a timeline to be shared. Council was also informed that the fireworks ordinance is postponed 
due to the need for a nexus study to justify fines, with the item expected to return early next year. The council 
referred the “Make Polluters Pay” Superfund Act to the Legislative Committee for review and possible 
recommendation to the full council in addition to considering a position on the upcoming Statewide Proposition 
50. Additionally, the council expressed strong support for formally recognizing Drew Diaz and Philip Gley, two 
local students who walked across the U.S. for charity.
ADJOURNMENT –The meeting adjourned at 10:24 p.m.

October 06, 2025 
SUBJECT:
City Council 2026 Regular Meeting Calendar — Adoption
RECOMMENDATION:
Adopt the City Council Regular Meeting schedule for the calendar year 2026 and, pursuant to Charter Section 2.10, 
authorize relocating the January 12 and January 26, 2026, Regular City Council Meetings to the Main Library.
BACKGROUND:
Each year, staff presents the City Council with a proposed calendar for regular meetings for the upcoming year. In 
accordance with the City Charter, regular City Council meetings are typically held on the first and third Mondays of each 
month, with exceptions for holidays. In July, August, and December, only one regular meeting is scheduled. Attachment 1 
lists the proposed 2026 Regular Meeting Calendar. Adjustments are proposed by staff to accommodate various holiday, 
religious, and cultural events.
Staff is currently managing the council chambers audio-visual replacement project, along with carpet repairs and 
replacements near the dais. These improvements will limit access to the chambers and prevent use for the first Council 
meeting of the new year, which is proposed to be scheduled for January 12, 2026. The project is anticipated to be 
completed the week of January 19, 2026.
Pursuant to Section 2.10 of the City Charter, all regular and adjourned regular meetings are to be held at City Hall unless 
the Council determines another location is more suitable due to its capacity or condition. In accordance with this provision, 
and to facilitate conduct of regular City business during the construction period, staff is requesting Council authorization 
for the January 12, 2026, and January 26, 2026, City Council meetings to be relocated to the Oak Room at the San Mateo 
Main Library.
BUDGET IMPACT:
There is no budgetary impact associated with this item. 
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This action is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an organizational or administrative activity that will not result in 
direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(5).)
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met.
ATTACHMENTS
Att 1 – Proposed Regular Meeting Calendar for 2026

SUBJECT:
Participation in National Opioid Settlement Agreement — Approval
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve the City’s participation in a no-cost opioid settlement agreement with Mylan and authorize the City Attorney to 
execute documents confirming the City’s participation and electing to have the settlement funds be provided directly to 
the City of San Mateo.
BACKGROUND:
On September 15, 2025, the City Council approved participation in opioid settlement agreements with Purdue Pharma, 
Alvogen, Amneal, Apotex, Hikma, Indivior, Sun and Zydus. This staff report requests participation in a settlement with 
Mylan, another opioid manufacturer, that was inadvertently omitted from the September 15 report to the Council. 
Over the last several years, a number of nationwide litigation matters have been filed against manufacturers, distributors, 
and retailers of opioids. The allegations in these lawsuits have generally been that the defendants were complicit in the 
increasing problem of opioid addiction in the United States, and that they knew or should have known that the products 
they made or sold were being misused. 
On December 6, 2021, the City Council first authorized the City Attorney to take all necessary steps and execute 
appropriate documents to participate in opioid settlement agreements with three opioid distributors – Cardinal Health, 
McKesson, and AmerisourceBergen (hereinafter, the “Distributors”) and the opioid manufacturer Janssen Pharmaceuticals, 
Inc., which is owned by Johnson and Johnson (collectively, “J&J”), and agree to implementing agreements. The City later 
joined settlement agreements involving Teva, Allergan, Walmart, CVS, Walgreens, and Purdue, among other entities.
The State of California has also come to a proposed settlement amount of $290 million with the opioid manufacturer 
Mylan. Like the other opioid settlements, local government support and sign-on are required to maximize the amount 
coming to our communities and eligible cities may elect to receive direct payment or have their allocated share go to the 
county in which they are located.
The amount the City will receive from these settlements is multi-factored and dependent on how many local agencies 
participate in the settlements. As an example, in 2022, the City Council authorized participation in a settlement agreement 
with J&J in the approximate amount of $820,000. From that settlement, the City was distributed approximately $28,000. 
Signing the participation agreement involving this opioid manufacturer will help direct settlement funds towards opioid 
mitigation efforts locally. If the City opts into the settlements, it must release its claims against all of these entities. The 
deadline to join this settlement with Mylan is October 8, 2025. 
If the City does not sign the participation agreement, then the funds will go to the State, but the total amount the State 
16 of 405

--- page 17 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
receives may be reduced since it is based on the number of cities and counties that participate. By not opting in, the City 
preserves the ability to litigate against the opioid distributors and manufacturers. 
These funds will go to the City if it joins the settlement and opts for direct payment. If the City joins the settlement but 
does not opt for direct payment, those funds will go to San Mateo County. Funds going directly to participating states and 
subdivisions must be used for pre-approved purposes designed to help abate the opioid epidemic. These include a wide 
range of intervention, treatment, education, and recovery services. If the City receives direct payment it is obligated to 
report on the use of the funds, which must be used primarily for opioid abatement. The funds received by the City to date 
have been used to offset the cost of a mental health clinician at SMPD. The clinician accompanies sworn police officers on 
calls for service involving individuals experiencing a mental health crisis because a significant number of these calls involve 
crises related to substance abuse, including opioids. 
BUDGET IMPACT:
There is no immediate budget impact for taking this action as it involves a decision whether to participate in a settlement 
agreement. Once the number of participating cities and counties is determined, a settlement administrator will calculate 
and distribute the settlement payment to the City. During fiscal year 24/25, the City received $186,141 in opioid payments 
from various settlement agreements in which the City Council previously authorized participation. 
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This proposed action is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an organizational or administrative activity that will not 
result in direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(5).)
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met.

SUBJECT:
Sycamore Tree Pruning – Agreement
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve an agreement with West Coast Tree Service, Inc. for sycamore tree pruning in the amount of $120,756; authorize 
a 10% contingency of $12,075, for a total amount not to exceed $132,831; and authorize the Director of Parks and 
Recreation to execute the agreement in substantially the form presented and issue change orders within the contingency 
amount.
BACKGROUND:
Staff identified 694 mature sycamore street trees throughout the city that need pruning to improve their form and 
enhance their longevity. A Request for Bids was published on the City's Bid Posting webpage on August 4, 2025. By the 
closing date of August 18, 2025, the City received six bids, the results of which were as follows: West Coast Tree Service, 
Inc.: $120,756.00- $174/tree; Davey Tree Experts: $161,008.00- $232/tree; West Coast Arborists: $224,856.00- $324/tree; 
Professional Tree Care: $267,190.00- $385/tree; California Tree Service: $291,480.00- $420/tree; and A Plus Tree Service- 
$410,848.00- $592/tree. Staff recommends that the agreement be awarded to West Coast Tree Service, Inc. based on the 
considerably lower bid amount, their background as a responsible contractor and based on their experience in pruning 
trees throughout Northern California. 
BUDGET IMPACT:
Funding for citywide tree pruning services is budgeted annually through the operating budget of the Park Department 
Arbor Division. There is sufficient funding in the fiscal year 2025-26 budget to cover the cost of this agreement. 
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This Project is categorically exempt from CEQA as an “existing facility,” because it consists of the operation, repair, 
maintenance, permitting, leasing, licensing, or minor alteration of existing public or private structures, facilities, 
mechanical equipment, or topographical features, involving negligible or no expansion of use. (CEQA Guidelines Section 
15301.)

All meeting noticing requirements were met.

name from mediators listed by either the American Arbitration Association, the State Mediation and 
Conciliation Service, or other agreed-upon service.  The mediator shall be selected by a blind draw.
The cost of mediation shall be borne equally by the parties.  Neither party shall be deemed the 
prevailing party.  No party shall be permitted to file a legal action without first meeting in mediation 
and making a good faith attempt to reach a mediated settlement.  The mediation process, once 
commenced by a meeting with the mediator, shall last until agreement is reached by the parties but 
not more than 60 days, unless the maximum time is extended by the parties.

EXHIBIT A
SCOPE OF SERVICES
Prune 694 Sycamore trees located throughout the city of San Mateo. All work shall be done in 
accordance with AZNI Pruning Standard and ISA Best Management practice to the following 
specifications:
•
Prune to reduce the canopy to 7-10ft to reduce end-weight. Pruning will occur in the outer 25% 
of the canopy.
•
Pruning of live branches should be between a diameter of two and four inches.
•
No more than one quarter of the canopy shall be removed.
•
Clean dead branches one inch in diameter and greater.
•
Mitigate hazards not visible from the ground.
•
Raise low limbs to 10 ft over sidewalks and 15ft over the road.
•
Clear surrounding structures by 3-5 ft.
The objective for pruning street trees is to achieve a structurally sound, low-risk condition, including sound 
structure, live branches, removal of chronic disease, and clearance for access and traffic control visibility; a 
uniformly shaped tree crown, while retaining as large a foliar crown size and leaf area as possible. 
Trees shall be pruned to achieve the objective based on the anticipated mature tree size, site conditions, 
available space, and current tree conditions. 
 Branches to be removed shall be selected to promote or retain a primary leader, acceptable branch aspect 
ratios, and consideration of the branch origination point as related to the portion of the crown the leaves 
occupy. The type of pruning cut to be performed shall be considered: 
•
Branch removal cut – removal of a whole branch back to the parent branch or trunk, leaving an intact 
branch collar. 
•
Reduction cut – a reduction of the length of a branch back to a lateral branch of equal or smaller 
diameter and large enough to assume the apical dominance. 
•
Heading cut – cutting a small twig back to a bud, cutting a branch back to a node without a lateral 
branch, or cutting a branch back to a lateral branch too small in diameter to assume apical dominance 
(less than 1/3 the diameter of the parent branch). 
Whenever reasonable, branch removal cuts and reduction cuts shall be preferred over heading cuts. Unless 
directed by the City to avert a high-risk situation, trees shall not receive a majority of heading cuts.
Defects that will remain after pruning operations shall be reported to the Managing Arborist or Tree 
Maintenance Specialist. Any structural weakness, decayed trunk or branches, split crotches or branches, shall 
be reported as soon as they are observed. If the detection of severe decay or split trunk or branches may 
change the assignment of pruning the tree, the pruning shall be stopped until the Managing Arborist/Tree 
Maintenance Specialist can review the findings and make a decision about the fate of the tree.

end-weight. Pruning will occur in the outer 25% of 
the canopy. Pruning of live branches should be 
between a diameter of two and four inches.
No more than one quarter of the canopy shall be 
removed. Clean dead branches one inch in 
diameter and greater. Mitigate hazards not visible 
from the ground. Raise low limbs to 10 ft over 
sidewalks and 15ft over the road. Clear surrounding 
structures by 3-5 ft.

end-weight. Pruning will occur in the outer 25% of 
the canopy. Pruning of live branches should be 
between a diameter of two and four inches.
No more than one quarter of the canopy shall be 
removed. Clean dead branches one inch in 
diameter and greater. Mitigate hazards not visible 
from the ground. Raise low limbs to 10 ft over 
sidewalks and 15ft over the road. Clear surrounding 
structures by 3-5 ft.
London plane 
tree (Platanus 
x hispanica)

removed. Clean dead branches one inch in

from the ground. Raise low limbs to 10 ft over

the canopy. Pruning of live branches should be 
between a diameter of two and four inches.
No more than one quarter of the canopy shall be 
removed. Clean dead branches one inch in 
diameter and greater. Mitigate hazards not visible 
from the ground. Raise low limbs to 10 ft over 
sidewalks and 15ft over the road. Clear surrounding 
structures by 3-5 ft.

No more than one quarter of the canopy shall be 
removed. Clean dead branches one inch in 
diameter and greater. Mitigate hazards not visible 
from the ground. Raise low limbs to 10 ft over 
sidewalks and 15ft over the road. Clear surrounding 
structures by 3-5 ft.

Prune to reduce canopy 7-10ft in order to reduce 
end-weight. Pruning will occur in the outer 25% of 
the canopy. Pruning of live branches should be 
between a diameter of two and four inches.

removed. Clean dead branches one inch in 
diameter and greater. Mitigate hazards not visible 
from the ground. Raise low limbs to 10 ft over 
sidewalks and 15ft over the road. Clear surrounding 
structures by 3-5 ft.

              EXHIBIT C
INSURANCE REQUIREMENTS
MINIMUM SCOPE OF INSURANCE 
Coverage shall be at least as broad as:
1. Commercial General Liability (CGL):  Insurance Services Office (ISO) Form CG 00 01 12 07 covering 
CGL on an “occurrence” basis, including products-completed operations, personal & advertising 
injury, with limits no less than $5,000,000 per occurrence. If a general aggregate limit applies, 
either the general aggregate limit shall apply separately to this project/location or the general 
aggregate limit shall be twice the required occurrence limit.
2. Automobile Liability: ISO Form Number CA 00 01 covering any auto (Code 1), or if Contractor has 
no owned autos, hired, (Code 8) and non-owned autos (Code 9), with limit no less than 
$1,000,000 per accident for bodily injury and property damage.
3. Workers’ Compensation: as required by the State of California, with Statutory Limits, and 
Employer’s Liability Insurance with limit of no less than $1,000,000 per accident for bodily injury 
or disease. 
If the contractor maintains higher limits than the minimums shown above, the City requires and shall be 
entitled to coverage for the higher limits maintained by the contractor.
Other Insurance Provisions
The insurance policies are to contain, or be endorsed to contain, the following provisions:
Additional Insured Status
The City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents are to be covered as insureds on 
the auto policy for liability arising out of automobiles owned, leased, hired or borrowed by or on behalf 
of the Contractor; and on the CGL policy with respect to liability arising out of work or operations 
performed by or on behalf of the Contractor including materials, parts or equipment furnished in 
connection with such work or operations. General liability coverage can be provided in the form of an 
endorsement to the Contractor’s insurance (at least as broad as ISO Form CG 20 10, 11 85 or both CG 
20 10 and CG 20 37 forms if later revisions used).
Primary Coverage
For any claims related to this contract, the Contractor’s insurance coverage shall be primary insurance 
as respects the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents. Any insurance or self-
insurance maintained by the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, or agents shall be 
excess of the Contractor’s insurance and shall not contribute with it.
Notice of Cancellation
Each insurance policy required above shall provide that coverage shall not be canceled, except after 
thirty (30) days’ prior written notice (10 days for non-payment) has been given to the City.
205 of 405

--- page 206 ---
Contract for Services SB854
Page 184 of 184
Rev 9/22
Waiver of Subrogation
Contractor hereby grants to City a waiver of any right to subrogation which any insurer of said Contractor 
may acquire against the City by virtue of the payment of any loss under such insurance.  Contractor 
agrees to obtain any endorsement that may be necessary to effect this waiver of subrogation, but this 
provision applies regardless of whether or not the City has received a waiver of subrogation 
endorsement from the insurer.  
Deductibles and Self-Insured Retentions
Any deductibles or self-insured retentions must be declared to and approved by the City. The City may 
require the Contractor to purchase coverage with a lower deductible or retention or provide proof of 
ability to pay losses and related investigations, claim administration, and defense expenses within the 
retention.  
Acceptability of Insurers
Insurance is to be placed with insurers with a current A.M. Best’s rating of no less than A:VII, unless 
otherwise acceptable to the City.
Verification of Coverage
Contractor shall furnish the City with original certificates and amendatory endorsements or copies of 
the applicable policy language effecting coverage required by this clause.  All certificates and 
endorsements are to be received and approved by the City before work commences.  However, failure 
to obtain the required documents prior to the work beginning shall not waive the Contractor’s 
obligation to provide them.  The City reserves the right to require complete, certified copies of all 
required insurance policies, including endorsements required by these specifications, at any time.

CITY OF SAN MATEO
CITY OF SAN MATEO

City Hall
330 W. 20th Avenue
San Mateo CA 94403

Agenda Number:  8
Section Name: CONSENT CALENDAR
Account Number: 82-4681
File ID: 25-10354
TO:
City Council
FROM:
Alex Khojikian, City Manager
PREPARED BY:
Public Works Department
MEETING DATE:
October 6, 2025 
SUBJECT:
Public Works Facilities Program Manager – Professional Services Agreement
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve an agreement with ArcPath Project Delivery, Inc. to provide professional program management services to the 
Public Works Facilities division from Fiscal Year 2025-26 through Fiscal Year 2027-28 in the amount of $300,000; and 
authorize the Public Works Director to execute the agreement in substantially the form presented and issue amendments 
within the agreement amount.
BACKGROUND:
Public Works staff requires the services of a professional program manager to assist the Public Works Facilities Division 
with the delivery of Capital Improvement and Maintenance projects. Currently, the division is without any Project 
Managers and has twenty-five active projects in various phases of development, design, permitting, and construction. 
There is an immediate need for a program manager that can provide services ranging from developing charters, procuring 
consultants and contractors, drafting, and coordinating construction and architectural consultation.
The program includes, but is not limited to, the following projects:
o
Transit Center Electrical Room Improvements 
o
City Hall UPS Replacement 
o
Police Station UPS Replacement
o
Corporation Yard Feasibility Study
o
2nd & El Camino Garage Feasibility Study
o
Tennis Court Garage Feasibility Study 
o
Main Street Garage Waterproofing 
o
Poplar Creek Clubhouse Waterproofing 
o
Central Recreation Center Roof Improvements
o
Beresford Recreation Center Roof Improvements
o
Senior Center Roof Improvements
o
City Hall Roof Improvements
o
Beresford Recreation Center Backup Generator 
o
Senior Center Backup Generator
o
Senior Center Fire Alarm System
o
2nd & El Camino Garage Fire Alarm System
o
City Hall Fire Alarm System Improvements
o
Main Library Lighting Controls Upgrade
o
Transit Center Elevator Modernization
207 of 405

--- page 208 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
o
Main Street Garage Elevator Modernization
o
Los Prados Park Emergency Field Lighting
o
Beresford Park Emergency Field Lighting
o
Citywide Court Resurfacing
o
Citywide Picnic Area Improvements
o
Citywide Fencing Improvements
o
Citywide Playground Equipment Replacement
o
Main Library Improvements
At the beginning of FY 2025–26, staff concluded that securing on-call program management services for a longer duration 
would be both effective and efficient. In July 2025, a Request for Proposals (RFP) was issued, outlining the specific criteria 
for providing program management services over a three-year term. On August 28, 2025, a total of nine (9) proposals were 
received and evaluated by staff based on factors such as relevant project experience, qualifications, and references. Based 
on the following evaluation results, staff recommends awarding the contract to ArcPath Project Delivery, Inc., which 
received the highest average score among all proposals.
Since ArcPath Project Delivery, Inc. has the requisite expertise, familiarity with this type of work, and experience with the 
City’s Facilities projects, staff recommends awarding a three-year agreement to ArcPath Project Delivery, Inc. through June 
2028.
BUDGET IMPACT:
There is sufficient funding available in each associated project’s budget to fund the cost of this agreement. 
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This project is categorically exempt from CEQA as an “existing facility,” because it consists of the operation, repair, 
maintenance, permitting, leasing, licensing, or minor alteration of existing public or private structures, facilities, 
mechanical equipment, or topographical features, involving negligible or no expansion of existing or former use. (CEQA 
Guidelines Section 15301.)

prevailing party.  No party shall be permitted to file a legal action without first meeting in mediation 
and making a good faith attempt to reach a mediated settlement.  The mediation process, once 
commenced by a meeting with the mediator, shall last until agreement is reached by the parties but 
not more than 60 days, unless the maximum time is extended by the parties.

EXHIBIT A
SCOPE OF SERVICES
Understanding of the Projects 
The City of San Mateo Public Works Department has been granted funding for various projects throughout the 
City. Due to a shortfall of internal resources, the department has been allowed to use the services of a third-
party consultant.
ArcPath Project Delivery, Inc. has been requested to assist with the programming and management of the 
design, bidding, and construction of these projects. The projects will generally be classified into one of two 
possible categories: 
•
Job Order Contracting Method: ArcPath assists with project oversight, coordination with Construction 
Procurement Services (Gordian), and Design Development / Construction Document level drawings with 
specifications to clarify scopes for pricing. Projects of this type may or may not be subject to Building 
Permits.
•
Design-Bid-Build Method: ArcPath assists with project oversight and overall coordination, but the 
complexity of the project requires the services of a separate professional design team. 
General Scope and Intent of the Scope of Services
The Scope of Services for owner representation and professional consultation services performed by ArcPath 
Project Delivery are outlined as follows: 
Various Capital Improvement Projects 
•
Review the general scope of an individual Capital Improvement Project to be implemented with Public 
Works Director, Deputy Director, and Facilities/Fleet Services Manager. 
•
Conduct or participate in meetings with users and stakeholders to review overall scope. 
•
Determine appropriate tasks required to deliver project. 
•
Develop and implement necessary communication tools such as scoping documents, schedules, drawing 
vignettes or sketches and budgets. 
•
Information from scoping documents and sketches is to be used for budget preparation. 
•
Communicate with facility staff or Construction Procurement Service representatives to develop a Work 
Plan and Bid/Cost Package. 
•
Coordinate contractor joint scope meetings to review project requirements, identify key details to be 
included in cost estimation phase. 
•
Identify potential cost savings measures with contractor during estimating phase. 
•
Develop construction documents suitable for pricing and permitting. 
•
Review design with Plan Check staff, Building Inspection, or other appropriate City/County personnel to 
obtain required permits. 
•
Construction documents prepared by ArcPath and submitted for permit review will either not require 
“wet seal and signed” documents, or the documents will be signed by a city staff member acting in the 
capacity of Engineer of Record. 
Parallel Tasks to be Completed with Work Plan Development/Staff Disruption Plan 
•
As Contractor Joint Scope Meetings are conducted, provide an analysis to determine how facilities and 
staff will be affected by construction work. 
•
Conduct meetings with Department supervisor(s) to review extent of staff disruption. 
219 of 405

--- page 220 ---
Professional Consultant Services
Page 9 of 13
Rev 5/25
•
Determine extent of construction interference on staff including but not limited to: Workplace 
environment relocations; IT/Communications – repositioning of computers, phones; provision of 
temporary facilities needed for staff to continue performing assigned tasks. 
•
When disruption extent is known, identify temporary facilities for relocation of staff. 
•
Develop scope of work for temporary facilities. 
•
Develop proposed construction schedule with Contractor. 
•
Review relocation plans and schedule with department staff and secure approval. 
Final Pricing, Contract and Construction Phase 
•
Define full work scope and review with Facilities Staff. 
•
Review comprehensive cost proposal in collaboration with Facilities Staff and present to appropriate 
City Departments and staff for review and approval. 
•
Upon receiving approval, coordinate the project start with Public Works and Facilities Staff and project 
inspector with selected Contractor. 
•
Distribute disruption plan for all City staff affected by construction work. 
•
Execute plan for temporary relocations as designed. 
•
If required, collaborate with IT Department for computer and communications relocations. 
The following tasks and site reviews with Contractors may or may not be performed by others: 
•
Construction inspection and quality control is performed by separate City Inspection staff. 
•
Once advanced preparation work is completed, relocate staff to temporary facilities. 
•
Commence work on main project with Contractor, monitor progress through site meetings and 
communications with City Staff and Inspector as needed to maintain updates. 
•
Review Submittals, Requests for Information and Substitutions submitted by the Contractor; provide 
recommendation/rejection to City staff for official response. 
•
Complete the construction project, follow through with Contractor on all closeout procedures. 
•
Upon completion of the renovation, coordinate the return of staff to reconstructed facilities. 
•
Upon vacating the temporary facilities, return the area to previous conditions, or as directed. 
Possible Various City Renovation or Facility Assessment Projects 
Proposed tasks will generally include the scope of services as listed above, except in addition: 
•
Collaborate with the staff of the selected design team to review the project program. 
•
Assist City Staff with oversight of assessment review or construction document production. 
•
Provide design team with Owner based information as requested, including but not limited to: Existing 
fixture/furniture specifications, dimensions, special requirements. 
•
Assist with communications between design team members, City departments, users, Public Works and 
Facilities managers, and Construction Procurement Service. 
General Intent of the Scope of Services 
Over the course of the work, tasks will be needed that are of an unknown quantity and duration, which may not 
be fully identified in the Scope of Services listed here. 
The intent is for the Program Manager Consultant to provide comprehensive project management services as 
needed and to identify all tasks required to complete the designated project. 
Due to the nature of the work, involvement and tasks can often change over the course of the project. Tasks 
generally remain within the parameters of the Scope of Services but depending on project needs the Program 
Manager Consultant will often perform additional services that were not anticipated at inception of the

reasonably possible within the requested fee.

EXHIBIT C
INSURANCE REQUIREMENTS
MINIMUM SCOPE OF INSURANCE 
Coverage shall be at least as broad as:
1. Commercial General Liability (CGL):  Insurance Services Office (ISO) Form CG 00 01 12 07 
covering CGL on an “occurrence” basis, including products-completed operations, personal & 
advertising injury, with limits no less than $2,000,000 per occurrence. If a general aggregate 
limit applies, either the general aggregate limit shall apply separately to this project/location or 
the general aggregate limit shall be twice the required occurrence limit.
2. Automobile Liability:  ISO Form Number CA 00 01 covering any auto (Code 1), or if 
CONSULTANT has no owned autos, hired, (Code 8) and non-owned autos (Code 9), with limit no 
less than $1,000,000 per accident for bodily injury and property damage.
3. Workers’ Compensation: as required by the State of California, with Statutory Limits, and 
Employer’s Liability Insurance with limit of no less than $1,000,000 per accident for bodily 
injury or disease. 
4. Professional Liability (Errors and Omissions): Insurance appropriate to the CONSULTANT’s 
profession, with limit no less than $1,000,000 per occurrence or claim, $2,000,000 aggregate.
If the CONSULTANT maintains higher limits than the minimums shown above, the City requires and 
shall be entitled to coverage for the higher limits maintained by the CONSULTANT.
Other Insurance Provisions
The insurance policies are to contain, or be endorsed to contain, the following provisions:
Additional Insured Status
The City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents are to be covered as insureds on 
the auto policy for liability arising out of automobiles owned, leased, hired or borrowed by or on behalf 
of the CONSULTANT; and on the CGL policy with respect to liability arising out of work or operations 
performed by or on behalf of the CONSULTANT including materials, parts or equipment furnished in 
connection with such work or operations. General liability coverage can be provided in the form of an 
endorsement to the CONSULTANT’s insurance (at least as broad as ISO Form CG 20 10, 11 85 or both 
CG 20 10 and CG 20 37 forms if later revisions used).
Primary Coverage
For any claims related to this contract, the CONSULTANT’s insurance coverage shall be primary 
insurance as respects the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents. Any 
insurance or self-insurance maintained by the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, or 
agents shall be excess of the CONSULTANT’s insurance and shall not contribute with it.
Notice of Cancellation
Each insurance policy required above shall provide that coverage shall not be canceled, except after 
thirty (30) days’ prior written notice (10 days for non-payment) has been given to the City.

SUBJECT:
Wastewater Treatment Plant Upgrade and Expansion Project – Contingency Reserve Increase
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve an increase to the contingency reserve to the construction agreement with Sundt Construction, Inc. for the 
Wastewater Treatment Plant Nutrient Removal and Wet Weather Flow Management Upgrade and Expansion Project in 
the amount of $773,702, for a total contingency amount of $61,193,702; and authorize the Public Works Director to issue 
change orders within the contingency amount. 
BACKGROUND:
The City is currently under a Regional Water Quality Control Board Cease and Desist Order requiring improvements to its 
sewer collection system and Wastewater Treatment Plant (WWTP) to eliminate sanitary sewer overflows and 
unauthorized discharges of untreated or partially treated wastewater to San Francisco Bay. The Clean Water Program 
(CWP) includes several capital improvement projects that are currently under construction and intended to comply with 
the Cease-and-Desist Order. The Wastewater Treatment Plant Nutrient Removal and Wet Weather Flow Management 
Upgrade and Expansion Project (GMP) is one of these projects, which will result in a new treatment plant for processing 
wastewater.
Due to the size and complexity of the project and construction demand in the Bay Area, a Construction Manager at Risk 
(CMAR) delivery approach was selected and approved by City Council on May 16, 2016. Sundt Construction, Inc. (Sundt) 
was the selected CMAR for the project. 
Construction of the project by Sundt has been underway since May 2019. Three construction packages were awarded: 
•
Package 1 - Site preparation: Work was substantially completed in July 2022. 
•
Package 2 - Foundation piles: Work was substantially completed in January 2022.
•
Package 3 - WWTP process facilities, Administration Building, and Maintenance Warehouse: In progress.
The current budget and contingency as of City Councill’s latest action of July 28, 2025, is as follows: 
Package # - General 
Description
Award Date

227 of 405

--- page 228 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
The CWP Annual Major Components (AMC) Projects includes several capital improvement projects that are currently 
under development or under construction and are intended to upgrade or rehabilitate aging infrastructure in the City’s 
sewer collection system and Wastewater Treatment Plant (WWTP). The AMC Project “3 Water Pumping Improvements 
and Ferric Chloride to Combine Sludge Line Project (AMC-NSI-06.3)” will be constructing improvements to the WWTP 3-
Water system, Storm Drain Retention System, and Ferric Chloride Chemical System. 
As part of the AMC-NSI-06.3 project, the project will be replacing the existing ferric chloride chemical tank with a smaller 
day tank, installing a new transfer pump in the recently constructed Area 70 (Chemical Area) of the new plant and 
constructing a new utility trench connecting Area 70 to the new day tank. If this new utility trench is constructed under 
this AMC project, it will occur after the completion of GMP-3. This would require cutting through brand new paving and 
landscaping installed under the GMP project. To prevent this future disruption, staff recommends for the utility trench to 
be removed from the scope of the AMC project, and to be installed as part of the scope of the GMP project prior to the 
paving and installation of landscaping in this area.
Increasing the contingency reserve in the amount of $773,702 associated with the Sundt contract will allow the utility 
trench work to be completed in alignment with the timeline of construction work currently underway in that location. 
BUDGET IMPACT:
Sufficient funds are not available in the Wastewater Treatment Plant Nutrient Removal and Wet Weather Flow 
Management Upgrade and Expansion (GMP (46t003)) project budget to fund this contingency increase to the agreement 
with Sundt. Funding for the AMC-NSI-06.3 project is budgeted in the CWP AMC Projects (AMC-NSI-06.3 (46t090)) and 
sufficient funds are available in this project to fund the contingency increase to the contract for the utility trench work 
associated with the project.  The awarded contract amount with Sundt for construction was in the amount of 
$430,694,974. The contingency reserve established was $60,420,000 and this request increases the contingency by 
$773,702 to a total of $61,193,702. This increase brings the potential total contract cost to $491,888,676.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
The City prepared a Final Programmatic Environmental Impact Report (Final PEIR) in accordance with the California 
Environmental Quality Act (CEQA) (SCH No. 2015032006). Council on June 6, 2016, certified the PEIR. In accordance with 
CEQA, the Final PEIR serves as the primary environmental compliance document for the implementation of the Clean 
Water Program. The City prepared Addenda to the Final PEIR that was approved on July 16, 2018 (Addendum 1) and April 
15, 2019 (Addendum 2). This work is within the scope of the Project evaluated in the PEIR and Addendum.

RECOMMENDATION:
Adopt a Resolution authorizing submittal of a grant application for the California Department of Resource Recycling 
(CalRecycle) and Recovery Rubberized Pavement Grant Program and designating the Public Works Director, or his/her 
designee, as the authorized signatory for a five-year term to sign the grant documents, including the grant agreement. 
BACKGROUND:
In August 2025, staff received notice that Cycle 18 of the California Department of Resource Recycling and Recovery’s 
(CalRecycle) Rubberized Pavement Grant Program (Grant) was open for application submission. The program provides 
opportunities to divert waste tires from landfill disposal, prevent illegal tire dumping, and promote markets for recycled-
content tire products by encouraging use of rubberized hot mix asphalt (RHMA). Projects that propose to place a minimum 
of 2,000 tons of RHMA are eligible to apply for the Grant. 
The City is currently in the design phase of the Citywide Street Rehabilitation Package 6B-2 Project (Project), which 
proposes approximately 5,000 tons of RHMA over six street segments. Staff anticipates bidding the Project in early 
summer of 2026 with construction anticipated to begin in the fall. Given the tonnage of RHMA anticipated to be placed, 
the Project may be eligible to receive up to $150,000 in Grant funds. 
To apply for the Grant, CalRecycle requires a Resolution that authorizes submittal of the Grant application, authorizes a 
signatory, and identifies the term of the authorizations. The Resolution also authorizes execution of a grant agreement, 
amendments, and requests for payment necessary to secure grant funds and implement the project.
Therefore, staff recommends City Council adopt the proposed Resolution approving submittal of the Grant application and 
designating the Public Works Director or his/her designee as the authorized signatory for a five-year term. If CalRecycle 
approves the City’s request for Grant funding, the funds will go towards the Project. 
BUDGET IMPACT:
Authorization of a grant application to CalRecycle Rubberized Pavement Grant Program requires no local match funding or 
additional expenses from the City. If awarded, this grant will provide funding for the Citywide Street Rehabilitation Package 
6B-2 project.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This Resolution is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an organizational or administrative activity that will not result 
in direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(5).)

SUBJECT:
Peninsula Corridor Multimodal Complete Streets Project — Grant Application
RECOMMENDATION:
Adopt a Resolution approving the submittal of a grant application for $1,125,000, with a local match in the amount of 
$245,000, to the San Mateo County Transportation Authority (SMCTA) for Highway Program Grant Funding for the 
Peninsula Avenue Multi-Modal Corridor Study; and authorize the City Manager to take any other actions necessary to 
receive grant funds including executing a supplemental agreement or amendment to the Primary Grant Agreement with 
the SMCTA and the City of Burlingame relating to funding for the project.
BACKGROUND:
The San Mateo County Transportation Authority (SMCTA) released a Call for Projects for grant funding from the Measures 
A and W Highway Program on July 11, 2025. The funds through this grant program may be used to support projects that 
improve supplemental roadway projects throughout the county. The City, in partnership with the City of Burlingame, is 
seeking $1,125,000 in funding to conduct the Peninsula Avenue Multi-Modal Corridor Study (Corridor Study).
Peninsula Avenue is shared between San Mateo and Burlingame, requiring close coordination on any planning efforts or 
roadway improvements. The Corridor Study, through a community engagement process, would identify improvements to 
enhance safety for all users, reduce vehicle delays through modernized traffic operations, and expand equitable access to 
sustainable transportation options. The study would evaluate improvements to strengthen regional connectivity by linking 
neighborhoods and multifamily complexes to five SamTrans stops, San Mateo High School, Washington Elementary School, 
businesses, and the Bay Trail, while also supporting climate and public health goals through increased opportunities for 
walking, biking, and transit use. The outcome of the Corridor Study is to develop a concept-level design which reflects 
community feedback and demonstrates shared buy-in for the proposed improvements. The study would look at the 
Peninsula Corridor from El Camino Real to Coyote Point Road on the other side of Highway 101, which will support active 
transportation connectivity to nearby recreational spaces and the Bay Trail for residents in a Metropolitan Transportation 
Commission (MTC) Equity Priority Community.  
 
The Peninsula Avenue corridor has been consistently prioritized for improvements through past planning processes and 
extensive engagement. Safety and multi-modal improvements are identified in the City of San Mateo’s Local Roadway 
Safety Plan (LRSP) and 2020 Bicycle Master Plan, both of which were developed with robust community outreach. 
Peninsula Avenue needs safer and more continuous facilities for pedestrians and bicyclists, suffers from outdated signal 
operations, and experiences congestion and safety challenges that limit multimodal mobility. Proposed improvements to 
be further vetted with the community include pedestrian scale lighting, which is recommended in the City’s Pedestrian 
Master Plan, and bicycle facilities, which are recommended in the City’s Bicycle Master Plan. The intersections of Peninsula 
Avenue with Delaware Street and Stanley Road are both identified as high priority locations for safety improvements in the 
City’s Local Roadway Safety Plan. Furthermore, the City/County Association of Governments (C/CAG) Local Roadway Safety 
232 of 405

--- page 233 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
Plan identifies Peninsula Avenue as part of the county’s Pedestrian High Injury Network. 
If awarded, the grant funding will be used for project planning, community outreach and public engagement, and 
preliminary engineering. Completion of these tasks will set the City up to proceed to project design. The City could seek 
additional funding for design and construction in future SMCTA grant cycles. Given the joint ownership of Peninsula 
Avenue with the City of Burlingame, and the intent is for both Cities to sponsor the grant application and provide matching 
funds. Burlingame staff has already secured a supporting resolution from the Burlingame City Council. The total cost of the 
proposed planning and preliminary engineering tasks for the Peninsula Corridor Multi-Modal Complete Streets Project is 
$1,500,000. If awarded, the grant requires a twenty-five percent (25%) local match. Staff from the City of San Mateo and 
City of Burlingame propose to share funding of the local match with San Mateo providing $245,000 and Burlingame 
providing $130,000, with the grant making up the remaining $1,125,000. The City of San Mateo’s share of the matching 
funds is higher because the City owns or operates a longer portion of Peninsula Avenue over the limits of the Corridor 
Study. Staff requests that Council adopt a resolution in support of the grant application and commit to providing the 
required matching funds if awarded the grant, as required by the Transportation Authority. 
BUDGET IMPACT:
The submittal of the grant application has no immediate financial impact. If awarded, the City of San Mateo will commit to 
providing $245,000 in matching local funds. Staff will allocate $215,000 in already budgeted funds from the Peninsula 
Corridor Complete Streets (46r029) project with the remaining $30,000 to be budgeted in the 2026-27 fiscal year capital 
improvement program.  
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
Adoption of this Resolution approving a grant application to the San Mateo County Transportation Authority is not a 
project subject to CEQA, because it is a government fiscal activity which does not involve any commitment to any specific 
project which may result in a potentially significant impact on the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(4).)

SUBJECT:
Peninsula Avenue and North Delaware Street Intersection Modification Project — Agreement
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve an agreement with Sandis, Inc. for the Peninsula Avenue and North Delaware Street Intersection Modification 
Project in the amount of $167,940; establish a contingency reserve in the amount of $17,000; and authorize the Public 
Works Director to execute the agreement in substantially the form presented and issue amendments within the approved 
contingency amount.
BACKGROUND:
Modifications are proposed for the traffic signal infrastructure at Peninsula Avenue/North Delaware Street/Dwight Road 
(Intersection) to improve pedestrian safety. The Intersection is located on the border of the Cities of San Mateo and 
Burlingame where the boundary runs along the centerline of Peninsula Avenue with Burlingame to the north and San 
Mateo to the south. 
The Intersection was identified as a Tier 1 priority intersection in the City’s Local Roadway Safety Plan (LRSP), ranking 7th of 
the top ten locations. Additionally, it is identified on the City and County Association of Governments (C/CAG) Pedestrian 
and Motor Vehicle High Injury Network (HIN). Improvements proposed with this project will align with the LRSP’s vision 
and goals and will include improving signal hardware, providing protected left turns, high visibility crosswalks, corner 
ramps, curb extensions, and consideration of sidewalk repair (where needed). Additionally, outdated signal infrastructure 
will be upgraded to current standards. 
A Request for Proposals (RFP) for design services for the project was posted to the City bid/proposal page on August 5, 
2025. Addendum No. 1 was issued on August 19, 2025. A total of six (6) proposals were received prior to the close of the 
submittal on August 26, 2025. Based on a review of the proposals, staff selected Sandis as the preferred consultant. In 
addition to being significantly lower in cost, the Sandis proposal provided important supplemental information about 
specific design challenges and potential solutions/mitigation. Lastly, Sandis also demonstrated a more comprehensive 
understanding of the goals of the project in relation to future plans for corridor improvements than the other consultants.
BUDGET IMPACT:
There are sufficient funds available in the Peninsula/Delaware Intersection Safety Improvement Project (46r031) to award 
this agreement for design professional services in the amount of $167,940 and to establish a contingency reserve of 
$17,000. 
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:

CITY OF SAN MATEO

maintenance, permitting, leasing, licensing, or minor alteration of existing public or private structures, facilities, 
mechanical equipment, or topographical features, involving negligible or no expansion of existing or former use. (CEQA 
Guidelines Section 15301.)

SECTION 19 - MEDIATION
Should any dispute arise out of this Agreement, any party may request that it be submitted to 
mediation.  The parties shall meet in mediation within 30 days of a request.  The mediator shall be

Conciliation Service, or other agreed-upon service.  The mediator shall be selected by a blind draw.

and making a good faith attempt to reach a mediated settlement.  The mediation process, once 
commenced by a meeting with the mediator, shall last until agreement is reached by the parties but 
not more than 60 days, unless the maximum time is extended by the parties.

EXHIBIT A
SCOPE OF SERVICES
Task 1 - Project Management and Coordination
Sandis will oversee project development to ensure quality deliverables by maintaining open 
communication with the City and monitoring the project schedule. This will include, but is not limited 
to, project meetings, regular updates, and general project management tasks.
Meeting agendas, presentations (if applicable), and draft notes will be circulated for each project 
meeting. Agendas and presentations will be provided at least 3 working days prior, and draft notes 
within 5 working days after. The City can review and request changes to notes before finalization.
Upon NTP, our team will schedule a kick-off meeting to establish lines of communication between the 
project team and City staff, discuss the detailed work plan, review the project schedule and budget, 
and discuss any logistical elements of the project, such as file sharing platform preferences and 
invoicing requirements. The kick-off meeting will include representatives of all firms on the design 
team, the City of San Mateo, and the City of Burlingame (as-available).
Following the project kickoff meeting, Sandis will schedule regular check-in meetings with City staff to 
provide project updates, discuss design challenges when they arise, and confirm adherence to the 
project schedule.
The Project Schedule included in this proposal anticipates completion of the bid package by April 28, 
2026. This schedule can be amended throughout the project to meet the City’s needs.
It is assumed that these check-ins will occur on a bi-weekly basis, but specific frequency and need shall 
be established in the Project Kick-off Meeting and be held virtually on a video call platform to be 
established in the project kickoff meeting. 
Task 1 Deliverables
• Kickoff Meeting Agenda and Meeting Notes (MS Word)
• Project Schedule and Updates (MS Project or MS Excel)
• Monthly Project Invoices (PDF)
Task 2 - Intersection Traffic Analysis and Design Scoping
Sandis will lead the effort to gather pertinent data and information, analyze existing conditions, and 
evaluate project alternatives. This is anticipated to include the following subtasks.
Task 2.1 - Topographic and Boundary Base Map
Sandis’ internal survey department will prepare a base map of the project area. The map will include 
the following elements:
247 of 405

--- page 248 ---
Design Professional Services 2024
Page 9 of 19
Rev 1/24
• Cross-sections every 20 feet for linear sections with the following minimum survey points: Terrain 
features such as grade breaks, swales, ditches, retaining walls, curb, gutter, sidewalks, and roadways.
• All significant features within the surveyed area, such as fences, walls, encroaching private 
improvements, trees, pavement markings, striping, signs, signal equipment, etc.
• Topographic lines and information including all points surveyed.
• Utility facilities including poles, structures and as-built information associated with underground 
facilities.
• All drainage facilities such as drainage ditches, valley gutters, concrete curbing, asphalt berms, 
swales, storm drain inlets and manholes shall be located. The center top and face of inlets structures 
shall be surveyed.
• All recorded monuments and recorded survey points that may be removed or disturbed during 
construction and that are required to be restored upon completion of the pathway construction work.
• Right-of-way limits shall be shown on the base maps.
The area to be surveyed will include the project intersection at Peninsula Avenue and Delaware 
Street/Dwight Road, as well as 120’ in each direction from the intersection, measured from the existing 
curb return (capturing the extents of all the existing turn lanes at the intersection).
This task will also include the gathering of existing data from relevant utility companies, the City of San 
Mateo, the City of Burlingame, and other relevant agencies. Sandis will lead the effort to make data 
requests from all of these agencies, and will utilize tools, such as the Civilgrid platform, to gather and 
output datasets where possible. A matrix will be created as a record keeping tool, which will identify all 
data requests sent, a history of outreach to the agencies, the source of all data received, and the type 
of data received. This matrix will be maintained throughout the project and provided to the City at all 
deliverable points if it has needed to be updated since the previous deliverable. 
Task 2.2 - Analysis of Existing Conditions, Phasing Plans, & Alternatives
Sandis will review the existing traffic counts that the City procured in February 2025. Sandis will also 
collect traffic counts through our partner count vendor, IDAX. It is currently anticipated that the counts 
will include AM, PM, and mid-day, and weekend peak hour multimodal turning movement traffic 
counts at the intersection, as well as 24 hour tube counts at the mid-blocklocation of all 4 legs of the 
intersection to better understand speed and volume classification breakdowns for the existing traffic. 
In addition to the traffic counts, Sandis will request existing timing cards and signal as-builts to 
understand the phasing, timing, coordination, detection, and settings of the existing signal system. The 
Sandis Team will also conduct a site visit as part of this effort to verify the existing equipment and 
collect photos. 
Using the data and information gathered above, Sandis will perform the intersection traffic analysis of 
the existing conditions. Following the analysis of the existing conditions, Sandis will develop up to three 
project alternatives to be further assessed and analyzed with (existing plus project alternatives) and 
without (future plus project alternatives) the proposed bike facilities from the Bicycle Master Plans of 
the two neighboring cities. These analyses will be used to identify potential operational deficiencies in 
the signal cycle for existing or future conditions, and identify solutions, which may include, but are not 
limited to, signal phasing changes, signal equipment changes/upgrades, and lane reconfigurations. 
248 of 405

--- page 249 ---
Design Professional Services 2024
Page 10 of 19
Rev 1/24
Sandis will use the Synchro program, and accompanying SimTraffic software to perform all traffic 
analyses. The analysis will utilize the Highway Capacity Manual (HCM) methodologies for estimating 
vehicle delays, queue lengths, and volume-to-capacity ratios for the intersection and each individual 
approach of the intersection.
Task 2.3 - Traffic Analysis and Operations Memorandum
The results of the analysis from Task 2.3 will be summarized in a technical memorandum addressed to 
the City. The memorandum will include summaries of the project background, existing conditions, 
explanation of procedures used for the analyses, proposed conditions, future conditions, and proposed 
mitigations. All traffic count summaries, Synchro reports, and queuing reports generated as part of this 
effort will be included as appendices to this memorandum. 
A draft memorandum will be submitted to the City for review, and the City will have the opportunity to 
provide a single set of consolidated, consistent comments, which Sandis will incorporate where 
appropriate to finalize the memorandum. The final memorandum will be submitted to the City, and 
utilized as an appendix for the Basis of Design in the following subtask.    
Task 2.4 - Basis of Design Memorandum
Sandis will develop a comprehensive Basis of Design memorandum that will outline the following 
elements: research, background, and data collected for the project; a summary of the stakeholder and 
outreach efforts, including results of the survey; a comparison of options and alternatives; tables and 
exhibits; preliminary cost estimates; design standards to be used for the development of the 
construction documents.
It is anticipated that this document will largely follow a format and layout similar to the Basis of Design 
that Sandis has prepared for previous projects with the City of San Mateo, such as 46R001 (Hillsdale 
Boulevard & Alameda de las Pulgas Traffic Signal Project).
A draft memorandum will be submitted to the City for review, and the City will have the opportunity to 
provide a single set of consolidated, consistent comments, which Sandis will incorporate where 
appropriate to finalize the memorandum. The final memorandum will be submitted to the City. The 
Final BOD will then be utilized to guide the development of the construction documents and will be 
referenced by the team at the start of every design phase to ensure adherence to the design standards 
established.
As part of the Basis of Design process, a preferred alternative will be selected and identified.
Task 2 Deliverables
• Topographic Survey and Base File (AutoCAD 2020 & PDF)
• Data Request Matrix (MS Excel) and received data files
• Traffic Count Reports (PDF)
• Traffic Analysis and Operations Memorandum [Draft and Final] (PDF, with appendices)
• Basis of Design Memorandum [Draft and Final] (PDF, with appendices)

Task 3 - Stakeholder and Community Engagement
Our Team will develop and implement a robust outreach workplan that responds to the diversity of 
community members and key stakeholders in and near the project area, including, but not limited to 
Spanish-speaking community members, North Central community members, City of Burlingame staff, 
and representatives from San Mateo Union High School District, San Mateo-FosterCity Unified School 
District, San Mateo Consolidated Fire, San Mateo Police Department, and Recology. Our Team, led by 
Winter, will support in the development of an outreach workplan that prioritizes equitable 
engagement and responds to various access, language and cultural needs in the community, leveraging 
engagement experience conducted prior, including for the San Mateo Complete Streets Plan, Complete 
Streets North Central Plan, and the Humboldt Street Bike Lane Alternatives Project. The engagement 
tactics that will be implemented include the following:
Project Webpage
At the commencement of the project, our Team will work with City of San Mateo staff to produce 
webpage content at or below an eighth-grade reading level and corresponding translations into 
Spanish that describes the project, its purpose, timeline, upcoming engagement opportunities and 
other relevant information for the community. Our Team will also work with the City to produce 
updated website content as necessary at the 50%, 90%, and 100% design submittal stages. 
Digital Materials
Our Team will work with the City of San Mateo staff to produce digital materials that will provide key 
updates to the community regarding project progress, upcoming engagement opportunities, survey, 
and engagement results, as necessary, at the start of the engagement period for the 50%, 90% and 
100% design submittal phases. This may include development of up to one social media graphic and 
one print flyer at each of the three phases for the various engagement opportunities and will provide 
pertinent information of how to access materials, including short links, QR codes, and key contact 
information. Materials will be developed with attention to various cultural and language sensitivities as 
outlined above. We will develop the content and design of digital materials for the City of San Mateo to 
distribute. 
Community Survey
At the early stage of the project, our Team will produce a digital survey that is easily comprehensible 
and accessible to a wide range of community members leveraging the Survey Monkey platform. The 
survey content will be produced at or below an eighth grade reading level with Spanish translations. 
Our Team will work with City of San Mateo staff to develop survey questions that will allow the project 
team to gather key and meaningful insights that will help the team identify the best solutions and 
improvements for the project. Our Team will provide analysis of results produced through the Survey 
Monkey platform analytics feature and share a list of all open-ended responses with the City in Excel or 
CSV format. We will also produce a print version of the survey that can be mailed and incorporated as 
a mailer for City of San Mateo staff to print and distribute. 
Key Stakeholder Virtual Focus Group
Our Team will facilitate a virtual focus group and work with the City of San Mateo staff to identify 
contacts and potential participants from key stakeholder groups, including, but not limited to San 
Mateo Union High School District, San Mateo-Foster City Unified School District, San Mateo 
250 of 405

--- page 251 ---
Design Professional Services 2024
Page 12 of 19
Rev 1/24
Consolidated Fire, San Mateo Police Department, and Recology. Contacts from each of the groups 
above will be invited to a virtual key stakeholder focus group to learn about the project and provide 
input on needs at the early stage of the project after the 50% design submittal phase and prior to the 
community workshop. Following, the participants will be asked to share word about the community 
workshop with their colleagues/constituents.
Community Workshop
Our Team will coordinate and implement one in-person community workshop at the 50% design 
submittal, including developing and printing workshop materials, including graphics, posterboards and 
flyers. The City of San Mateo will be responsible for printing and distribution the flyers to the 
approximately 7,500 residents that live within a ½ mile radius of the project site. As Spanish-speaking 
community members are a prevalent component of the project area, our Team will be sure to provide 
materials in both Spanish and English and will have Spanish-speaking staff at the workshop to support 
monolingual Spanish-speakers via a small group breakout in Spanish should any Spanish-speaking 
community members attend. The community workshop will provide an opportunity for all community 
members to learn about the project, hear what has been heard in terms of needs as gathered from the 
community survey, and provide feedback on initial design concepts for the project. Our Team will work 
to ensure that the workshop provides an opportunity for all voices to be heard in a civil dialogue that is 
respectful of a diversity of opinions and perspectives.
Simultaneous interpretation and corresponding interpretation devices are not incorporated into this 
item, but may be added for an additional cost.
Sustainability and Infrastructure Commission Meeting
At the 50% design submittal phase, our Team will prepare a presentation for the Sustainability and 
Infrastructure Commission meeting. At this meeting, our Team will provide a brief overview of results 
and insights gathered from previous community engagement activities, including feedback gathered 
from the community workshop, and key stakeholder focus group. We will present initial design 
concepts and gather input from the Commission. At the close of the Commission meeting, our Team 
will create a simple matrix of main feedback themes received, responses to each point, and 
recommended action items for the City staff for further development of project plans.
Task 4 - Develop Traffic Signal PS&E Documents
Sandis will prepare the bid ready construction documents for the project. The PS&E phase will consist 
of the following submittals:
• 50% (Plans, Draft Specifications, and Estimate)
• 90% (Plans, Specifications, and Estimate/Bid List)
• 100% Final (Plans, Specifications, and Estimate/Bid List)
We assume that 20 working days are needed for City review of 50% and 90% submittals and 15 
working days for City review of all other submittals. Comments will be provided in a single consolidated 
set of redlines. Our team will also be available to attend plan review “page turners” if needed, to 
expedite plan review.

--- page 252 ---
