October 6, 2025 
SUBJECT:
Gas Leaf Blower Prohibition — Update
RECOMMENDATION:
Provide direction on how to update the leaf blower Ordinance to prohibit the use of gas leaf blowers.
BACKGROUND:
Gas leaf blower regulations can help reduce greenhouse gas emissions and address air quality impacts. Many cities in the 
Bay Area have adopted gas leaf blower bans including the City of Burlingame, Town of Hillsborough, City of Menlo Park, 
and City of Palo Alto. At the April 3, 2023 City Council meeting, City Council decided not to pursue leaf blower regulations, 
and instead Council directed staff to develop a more robust rebate program, enhance community outreach and 
engagement on existing regulations and encourage the use of electric leaf blowers, and lead by transitioning City 
operations to electric leaf blowers. That was the most recent direction to staff until the February 2025 City Council Blue 
Sky meeting, when staff was directed to “Develop and implement an ordinance to prohibit the use of gas leaf blowers 
within the City of San Mateo” in the upcoming Fiscal Year. This report provides an overview of the City’s current leaf 
blower regulations, an update on the City’s rebate program and outreach, and an update on City operations. Finally, this 
report outlines policy areas for City Council to provide feedback in order for staff to proceed with an Ordinance prohibiting 
gas leaf blower use and recommendations from the Sustainability and Infrastructure Commission.
STATE AND CITY LEAF BLOWER REGULATIONS
State Regulations (AB 1346)
Small Off-Road Engine (SORE) includes equipment such as leaf blowers and lawnmowers. These engines present concerns 
for air pollution, noise pollution, and climate change. AB 1346 requires new SORE Model Years 2024 and later to be zero 
emission. The state regulation does not impact older gas equipment that is already in use and older gas equipment can still 
be purchased. 
City’s Current Regulations
San Mateo Municipal Code Chapter 10.80 “Operation of Leaf Blowers” (see Attachment 2) limits the use of leaf blowers to 
8:00 am to 5:00 pm on weekdays and 9:00 am to 5:00 pm on Saturdays. The use of leaf blowers is prohibited on Sundays 
and certain designated holidays. The hours of operation apply to residential zoning districts and in areas bordering 
residentially zoned neighborhoods. Uses of leaf blowers in residential zoning districts, or areas bordering residential zoning 
districts, also require the operator to use a blower nozzle extension and operate the leaf blower at a low speed to 
minimize noise. No more than one leaf blower may be operated at a residence at any time. Material blown by leaf blowers 
cannot be blown onto neighboring properties or onto the public right-of-way without being immediately removed. These 
restrictions have been in place since 1997. 
347 of 405

--- page 348 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
CITY’S ELECTRIC LEAF BLOWER REBATE PROGRAM
The City provides up to 75% of the purchase price up to a maximum of $500 to landscaping businesses and up to 50% 
purchase price and maximum of $100 for residents. At the time of writing this report, the City had issued 20 rebates to 
businesses and 97 rebates to residents since the program launched in 2021. The average residential rebate was $79.52 and 
the average business rebate was $399.94. The City spent an average of $3,142 per year on rebates. Historically, there has 
been ample budget to fund the rebate program. Since the City has not had a gas leaf blower prohibition in place, looking 
forward staff will closely monitor and evaluate the budget during the upcoming transition.
Per City Council’s direction in 2023, staff evaluated the City’s rebate program and staff did not increase the electric leaf 
blower rebate amount for a few reasons. Because state regulations require all new 2024 model year leaf blower 
equipment to be electric, the current rebate is not needed to incentivize the purchase of new electric equipment, as it is 
already required to be electric. Also, cost is not the only barrier for landscaping businesses to convert to the electric 
option. In staff’s 2023 outreach on the issue, landscaping businesses identified battery life and equipment performance as 
the leading barriers to using electric equipment. Note, a commercial landscaping business could potentially leverage 
multiple local rebates since other neighboring cities such as the City of Burlingame, City of Menlo Park, Town of Atherton, 
City of Redwood City and Town of Hillsborough also have electric leaf blower rebate programs. 
INCREASED COMMUNITY ENGAGEMENT AND OUTREACH
Staff has focused on increased engagement and marketing of the electric leaf blower rebate program which has helped 
increase rebate uptake. The rebate program participation was a record high of 46 rebates in 2024 compared to previous 
years with an average of 23 rebates per year.  Staff routinely sends paper mailers to the roughly 100 landscaping and 
gardening businesses with San Mateo business licenses. To broaden engagement, staff reached out to Home Depot and 
the Workers Resource Center. Staff also promoted rebates through the City’s e-newsletter, City’s social media channels 
and Recology bill insert. Staff’s recent outreach highlighted both the upcoming gas leaf blower prohibition ordinance as 
well as the City’s electric leaf blower rebate program. Continued outreach will be a key part of the transition after an 
ordinance is in place.
CITY OPERATIONS
Parks and Public Works staff and City contractors use leaf blower equipment to remove debris throughout the City. Parks 
staff rely on leaf blowers almost daily as a primary source to remove debris from pathways and parking lots. Public Works 
staff primarily use blowers during weed abatement and leaf season. In 2024, staff identified Peninsula Clean Energy (PCE) 
Member Agency Grant funding to fund the purchase of 23 electric leaf blowers, 92 batteries and 16 battery chargers for 
Parks operations. The Parks equipment was delivered in August 2025 and Parks staff began using electric equipment 
citywide in September 2025. Public Works staff use five electric backpack blowers and two electric handheld blowers. Staff 
are currently working with the City’s various contractors to transition to electric leaf blower equipment.
In 2023, Parks Division evaluated their operations equipment to determine a feasible starting point and transition plan to 
convert to electric operated tools. An electrical upgrade was completed at the Park Yard for equipment charging. Also in 
2023, Parks staff acquired a large area sweeper called a Multihog Compact Sweeper, thereby reducing the need for as 
much backpack blower cleanup work of parking lots and some pathways. The Multihog Compact Sweepers saves an 
estimated 14 hours of labor per week.  
POLICY RECOMMENDATIONS NEEDED
To update the City’s existing leaf blower regulations, staff seek City Council feedback in the following areas: 
Hours of Operation - Residential zoned areas vs. Citywide
The City’s currently adopted leaf blower regulations and the hours of operation limitations only apply to residential zoning 
districts and in areas bordering residentially zoned neighborhoods. There are residences in Transit Oriented Development 
(TOD) zones and in Downtown, where the City’s current leaf blower regulations hours of operation do not apply. The City 
could consider applying leaf blower hours of operation citywide. 
There is a lot of variation in how cities apply the hours of operations. The City of Menlo Park’s hours of operation apply 
348 of 405

--- page 349 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
citywide (Monday-Friday 8:00 am – 6:00 pm) and permits residents/property owners to use leaf blowers (Saturday, 
Sundays, and holidays 9:00 am – 5:00 pm). The City of Palo Alto has different hours of operation with residential zones 
having narrower hours of operation (Monday-Friday 9:00 am - 5:00 pm, Saturday 10:00 am - 4:00 pm) than non-residential 
zones (Monday-Friday 8:00 am - 6:00 pm, Saturday 10:00 am - 4:00 pm). 
If the City were to expand regulations to apply citywide, this would likely have an impact on commercial businesses and 
City operations where leaf blowers are used to clear debris from parking lots early in the morning. For example, the City 
uses a contractor to maintain Downtown garages that use leaf blowers before 7:00 am, an optimal time to avoid conflict 
with cars. The same is true of existing commercial and office properties, some of which are near locations which may be 
suitable for housing now or in the future even if they are not currently developed with housing. 
Staff seeks City Council feedback on how to proceed with revising the ordinance and whether to apply the hours of 
operation citywide or to continue with the existing approach where hours of operation apply to residentially zoned 
neighborhoods and in areas bordering residentially zoned neighborhoods.
Enforcement phasing
Staff reached out to cities with gas leaf blower bans and received feedback that ordinance enforcement is the primary 
challenge with leaf blower regulations. Unlike other code violations (e.g., inoperable vehicles, overgrown vegetation), the 
use of a leaf blower is fleeting in nature. Furthermore, the Code Enforcement Officer must personally observe the 
Municipal Code violation in order to enforce it. If staff is unable to witness the code violation, staff can use this 
opportunity to provide a courtesy letter with information about the new regulation.  
It is best practice for local jurisdictions to adopt an Ordinance and delay the Ordinance enforcement date to allow 
community members and landscaping businesses to transition to compliant electric leaf blower equipment. The City of 
Burlingame began enforcement 9 months after Ordinance adoption and the City of Menlo Park began enforcement 12 
months after Ordinance adoption. Staff recommends beginning enforcement of the Ordinance a minimum of 9 months 
after the Ordinance adoption date to allow for sufficient transition time. During this transition time, staff would conduct 
broad communitywide outreach about the new gas leaf blower prohibition. Staff seeks a recommendation from City 
Council on the Ordinance enforcement date.
Assignment of Penalties
San Mateo Municipal Code Chapter 1.10 Administrative Citations describes procedures that the City may pursue to 
address code violations through the issuance of administrative citations. The typical process includes the issuance of a 
warning prior to a citation. Citations begin at $100 and escalate to $200, and $500 per occurrence if not corrected. Other 
cities also rely on their administrative citations for their gas leaf blower Ordinance enforcement.
Other cities with gas leaf blower prohibitions include the option to enforce penalties against the owners of the property or 
any other responsible party who uses gas leaf blowers or have hired, employed, or engaged the services of a person or 
business utilizing gas leaf blowers. This way staff has multiple options to enforce penalties against other responsible 
parties beyond the leaf blower operators. Staff seeks City Council feedback on this approach to administering penalties for 
violations.
Sustainability and Infrastructure Commission Policy Recommendation
At the September 10, 2025 Sustainability and Infrastructure Commission meeting, staff presented a similar report and 
asked for the Commission  to make recommendations on the three policy areas described above. The Commission 
recommended 1) hours of operation apply to residentially zoned areas and areas adjacent to residential zones, 2) 
enforcement of the Ordinance to begin nine months after Ordinance adoption, and 3) penalties should be assigned to the 
homeowner or property owner, with the option to assign penalties to the leaf blower operator or any other responsible 
party, especially in situations when there is a commercial operator. In their discussion about the hours of operation, 
commissioners noted that allowing leaf blower activity in commercial areas outside of typical business hours is important 
because it is a safety issue, and helps keep landscapers safe by reducing risk and conflict with vehicles. Commissioners also 
349 of 405

--- page 350 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
pointed out that one of the tradeoffs of living in a vibrant and active Downtown or mixed-use area is embracing a higher 
level of noise. Commissioners were supportive of beginning enforcement nine months after Ordinance adoption and 
emphasized the need for strong messaging and education prior to the enforcement date.  
REQUESTED CITY COUNCIL DIRECTION 
Staff requests City Council direction on the following:
1.
Should the Ordinance apply electric leaf blower hours of operation to residential zones and areas adjacent to 
residential zones only, or expand the application of electric leaf blower hours of operation citywide?
2.
Should enforcement of the Ordinance begin 9 months, 12 months, or at a different time after Ordinance adoption? 
3.
Should the Ordinance include the option to enforce penalties against the property owners and/or any other 
responsible party who uses gas leaf blower or have hired, employed, or engaged the services of a person or 
business utilizing gas leaf blowers? 
4.
Does the City Council have other recommendations for the Ordinance prohibiting gas leaf blower use?
NEXT STEPS
Staff will incorporate City Council’s direction for the update of an Ordinance prohibiting gas leaf blower use. Staff 
anticipates Ordinance adoption in early 2026. Ordinance enforcement phasing will depend on City Council direction and 
timing.
BUDGET IMPACT:
The implementation and enforcement of this Ordinance would be integrated into the City’s existing code enforcement 
procedures. If City staff were directed to provide enhanced enforcement, this would require an assessment and allocation 
of staffing resources. On average, the City has issued 23 electric leaf blower rebates and amounting to an average of 
$3,142 per year, supported by the City’s Sustainability Program budget. Staff anticipate budgeting $10,000 per year for 
electric leaf blower equipment and battery replacement in future budget cycles. 
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This Council action in receiving an informational update and providing feedback for the development of an Ordinance 
prohibiting gas leaf blowers and additional leaf blower regulations is not a “project” subject to CEQA review, in that it 
consists of the planning for possible future actions which the City has not approved, adopted, or funded. (CEQA Guidelines 
Section 15262.)
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met. The City sent a mailer to landscaping businesses with a City of San Mateo 
business license to alert them of the September 10, 2025 Sustainability and Infrastructure Commission meeting, this 
October 6, 2025 City Council discussion, and the City’s Electric Leaf Blower Rebate Program.

Re: leaf blower ordinance in san mateo 
 
 
 
 
January 2025 
While Leaf Blowers are secondary in priority to matters like housing, they should be 
addressed in some way and follow the trend set by CARB ban on SORE.  I can’t imagine 
anyone lamenting the reduction of leaf blowers in the city.   For most residents it is a matter 
of noise.  The other eKects of LB are harder to discern.   There are studies showing the 
eKects of noise and increased stress levels.  European cities have a war on excessive noise 
with some putting sensors around the city to ﬁnd and eliminate the sources.  
• Noise (and secondary psychological eKects) 
• Turbidity (the stirring up of PM 2.5 particles which can lodge in the lungs, dust)§ 
• Worker Health (fumes from gas equipment, noise, repetitive stress injuries, noise) 
• Soil Erosion and compaction (blowing soil away)§  
• Air Pollution from ICE (1 hour of operation emits C02 on par with a long car drive) 
§ true of electric powered leaf blowers as well. 
We’ve come to accept this machinery as necessary but prior to 1990 leaf blowers were not 
used. So we know that rakes and brooms will work – but sometimes will take additional job 
time.  Let’s also recognize that people who pay landscapers are not in low-income bracket 
– this law would not negatively aKect low-income residents.  Most of the cities with bans 
are aKluent.  Perhaps a solution lies in moderation, but a simpler solution (total ban) is 
easier to explain.   Violations seem to be the diKicult part.  Burlingame (population 30,000) 
does it with the code compliance oKice. 
Cost 
I have not seen a comprehensive cost analysis but gas leaf blowers for commercial use 
cost about $600 plus fuel and maintenance while an electric setup will run about $2K with 
four batteries. So it’s really that $1200 diKerence. 
 
Number of landscapers 
San mateo has about 40,000 homes.  How many gardeners work here? I used an estimate 
of 10,000 homes which would be on the high side. If a crew of two can handle 50 
customers a month (visting every other week) we have about 200 landscapers working in 
the city.   Rough guess. 
 
Commercial 
I’ve been talking with landscapers and others about this for the past decade or so and have 
come to believe that for large concrete surfaces as found in commercial, leaf blowers can 
be an appropriate tool.

Re: Leaf blower operating costs to gardening ﬁrms 
 
Much has been written about the successful of LB (leaf blower) ordinances in local cities.   
A signiﬁcant encumbrance has been enforcement – but those details are working 
themselves out.  I am resending my memo of January 2025 which references the PIRG 
study showing a map of local cities.    
https://www.google.com/maps/d/u/0/viewer?ll=32.6969158138562%2C-
112.95336895&z=4&mid=1WlGTHOfzAcXHpxLZpEK43pfzSStxg90 
The primary drivers for LB for SORE landscaping equipment ordinances are noise reduction 
(to the worker and the community); Decreasing turbidity (which creates a semi-permanent 
dust cloud in neighborhoods) Reduction in Soil Erosion and dry earth compaction; and air 
pollution from high-speed ICE (internal combustion engines).    
Gardening has become hyper mechanized.  With some training we can reduce turbidity and 
soil compaction through the increase in use of hand tools such as rakes. The matter of 
worker health should be given signiﬁcant weight (fumes, ﬁres, repetitive stress injuries, 
noise).    
My suggestion last go around with SIC was to begin a conversation with our residential 
gardening workforce by oiering them rakes in exchange for completing a short online class 
on how to use a leaf blower.   Perhaps couple this with a reduced fee / amnesty for business 
licenses. I recall that SIC decided to oier $500 to residents who purchased leaf blowers.  It 
would be worth reviewing the results of that program.  I think that it opened the door on the 
conversation but didn’t sway many landscapers to convert. I learned that Palo Alto and Los 
Gatos have not paid them for ELB equipment despite ﬁlling out all the forms.   There is a 
lack of trust.

9/2/25 
2 
We need to hear from the business managers of these small businesses.  I encourage the 
city to create a working group with a half dozen representatives.   I took it upon myself to 
talk with several landscapers about the new Stihl models.  It takes a little more time on 
each job.  The main complaint is weight.  The battery life is borderline acceptable because 
they don’t need to run at full capacity and can rake more.  For the worksheet I assumed two 
battery packs and two chargers. The electric equipment from a few years ago has had 
mechanical issues.   
The lack of fumes and lower noise / vibration makes the job less stressful.  We would have 
to consult with a landscaper and a Stihl dealer to get  real-world numbers.   I have assumed 
mow and blow (high volume quick service).  “Artisanal” gardeners are not time driven and 
tend to make better use of rakes.   MFH is diierent from SFH because of the large concrete 
spaces and consistent landscaping.   There is  an argument that raking takes longer than 
blowing – but blowing with electric should require the same amount of time as SORE. 
I spoke with our landscaper.  $4500-$5000 per truck is about right.  Each truck has a two or 
three person crew (almost exclusively male).   Compare this to a new gas powered (around 
$750), and realize their perspective on costs. If there were no increased costs ELB would be 
a no brainer.   In Palo Alto, they raised their annual rate, but only about 20% of the houses 
are in areas with LB bans. 
Below ﬁnd a structure for determining equipment costs, number of contractor crews for 
the city of San Mateo.  They service about 50 houses a month per truck.   This leads to the 
conclusion that cost is shouldn’t be a signiﬁcant impact.  $25 / year per customer for four 
years.   Business licenses run between $1000 and $3000 per city.  Perhaps the city can 
reduce the business license fees to oiset new requirements for equipment.

S and I Commission,
Regarding the proposed leaf blower ordinance:
 
1. I would like a city-wide ban on the use of gas-powered leaf blowers, following the example of
other cities in San Mateo County – with NO  exemptions. Zoning is complex, ineffective, and not
equitable.
2. Because the good health of the workers and our residents must be the highest priority, I
would like the ordinance to become effective on January 1, 2026. I would like courtesy notices to
be sent out immediately to property owners and businesses when violations are reported via
citizen affidavits.
3. I would like the Code Enforcement department to have the discretion to levy fines against the
responsible party. The property owner would be the primary responsible party. An employee
who operates this equipment at the direction of business management would not be considered
to be responsible.
4. I would like the city to adopt the draft ordinance language submitted by Quiet Clean San
Mateo.
https://docs.google.com/document/d/1cPTFiLp8c6yFbYQLazPhuMysTvvvTuCy_v051izv9To/edit?
usp=sharing
5. I do NOT support using City funds for a rebate program to buy electric blowers. The
impending ordinance has been discussed for many years and the City has a deficit.  
Rick Sakuda 
San Mateo, CA

Public Comment
Sustainability & Infrastructure Commission Members, 
Thank you for reviewing this critical public health and sustainability 
issue. Quiet Clean San Mateo would like to offer our support on the 
important questions the City Council has raised. 
The primary driver for this change is public health. Countless people are 
suffering from gas-leaf blowers harms every day, especially the workers 
who use them. We need change urgently, without unnecessary delay.  
The City Council has asked the Sustainability & Infrastructure 
Commission the following questions.
1. 
Does the Commission recommend applying leaf blower hours of 
operation to residential zoned and adjacent to residential zoned 
areas or expanding the leaf blower hours of operation to apply 
citywide?
2. 
Does the Commission recommend beginning enforcement of the 
ordinance 9 months, 12 months, or later after ordinance adoption?
3. 
360 of 405

--- page 361 ---
Does the Commission recommend that the ordinance include the 
option to enforce penalties against the property owners and/or any 
other responsible party who uses gas leaf blower or have hired, 
employed, or engaged the services of a person or business utilizing 
gas powered leaf blowers?
We will offer recommendations for each. 
We support extending existing hours of operation to the entire city. 
The revised ordinance language would be “No person shall use or 
operate a leaf blower before 8:00 a.m. or after 5:00 p.m. Monday 
through Friday, nor prior to 9:00 a.m. or after 5:00 p.m. on Saturdays,” 
with prohibition on Sundays and holidays. This keeps the rules simpler 
and easier for businesses to follow. It plans for the future needs of the 
city and respects people already living in denser areas, such as 
downtown, who especially need quiet early in the morning. We 
understand there will be some challenges with new operating hours, but 
we would ask contractors to adapt to the community’s needs, not the 
other way around. 
We support beginning enforcement in no more than 9 months. This 
is an urgent public health matter, so we disagree with the 9 month 
delay. However, we understand it. We recommend that, in the 
meantime, staff accepts complaints and sends courtesy notices. That 
will afford plenty of advance notice and opportunities for targeted 
feedback. 
In staff’s 2023 outreach on the issue, landscaping businesses identified 
battery life and equipment performance as the leading barriers to using 
electric equipment. In other words, landscapers need to break the old, 
bad habits they developed while using gas-powered leaf blowers. With 
gas, you could get away with revving the engine as you walked around 
the property, using full power at all times, even if that made a bigger 
mess than you started with, and using the blower everywhere, even if 
there was virtually no debris to remove. 
361 of 405

--- page 362 ---
With electric leaf blowers, you must use only the power you need, and 
use the blower only when it helps you. That will save battery life, reduce 
the number of batteries you need to buy, and make the transition much 
easier. 
Our recommendation is the city’s outreach program emphasizes this 
practical advice. We also recommend explaining why the city has made 
this change. This is not something the community is doing to 
landscapers, but for them. They want to go home at the end of their 
workday not smelling so much like exhaust and with their ears buzzing, 
and the community is supporting that.
We support the option to cite the property owner. The owner 
ordered the service and is responsible for what happens on their 
property. They have leverage to change their service requirements, 
reducing burden on the community and/or city staff. Holding the 
property owner responsible makes sense. We do not support citing the 
person holding the tool, unless they are the landscaping business 
owner. 
Property owners can be shown why this change benefits them - surely 
they don’t want clouds of toxic fumes around their homes - and 
landscapers can be given the practical guidance noted earlier.
Regarding enforcement challenges, violations can be reported by San 
Mateo residents on the existing website 
(https://www.cityofsanmateo.org/FormCenter/Reporting-a-Problem-
15/Report-a-Code-Violation-139). There is no need for code 
enforcement to witness gas leaf blower violations, and the citation 
process can be automated. 
In our conversations with California cities, we found some places 
making enforcement very hard on themselves. The code enforcement 
officer was sometimes left with too many judgment calls to make, and 
they hesitated to be the “bad guy.” While understandable, that makes 
things harder on everyone. Once some party has been given a warning, 
362 of 405

--- page 363 ---
and some feedback on what to do differently, it is fair to move on to a 
fine. 
In summary, we support simple rules and procedures. The grace period 
before the ordinance takes effect is a wonderful opportunity to explain 
why we have made this change, and give anyone who is struggling a 
boost. When the community works together, we all win. 
Quiet Clean San Mateo
363 of 405

City of San Mateo Law Library / City of San Mateo Municipal Code / Title 10 PEACE, SAFETY AND
MORALS / Chapter 10.80 OPERATION OF LEAF BLOWERS
Chapter 10.80 OPERATION OF LEAF BLOWERS
10.80.010 PURPOSE.
It has been found that leaf blowers cause considerable noise and air pollution and have been the source
of numerous complaints by San Mateo citizens living in residential zoning districts. This chapter is
intended to regulate the use of leaf blowers to minimize noise and air pollution in the City's residentially
zoned neighborhoods and in areas bordering residentially zoned neighborhoods.
(Ord. No. 1997-2 § 1.)
10.80.020 LEAF BLOWER—DEFINITION.
Leaf blowers are defined as portable equipment that is powered by a self-contained fuel engine and
used in any landscape, maintenance, construction, property repair, or property maintenance for the
purpose of blowing, dispersing or redistributing dust, dirt, leaves, grass, clippings, cuttings and trimmings
from trees, shrubs or other debris.
(Ord. No. 1997-2 § 1.)
10.80.030 HOURS OF OPERATION.
No person shall use or operate a leaf blower in a residential zoning district or in areas bordering a
residential zoning district before 8:00 a.m. or after 5:00 p.m. Monday through Friday, nor prior to 9:00
a.m. or after 5:00 p.m. on Saturdays. Use of leaf blowers on Sundays or on the following holidays is
9/26/25, 6:17 PM
City of San Mateo Law Library
about:blank
1/3
364 of 405

--- page 365 ---
prohibited: New Years Day, Martin Luther King, Jr. Birthday, Presidents' Day, Memorial Day, 4th of July,
Labor Day, Veterans Day, Thanksgiving, Christmas.
(Ord. No. 1998-6 § 1; Ord. No. 1997-2 § 1.)
10.80.040 LIMITATIONS ON USE.
Any person who uses or operates a leaf blower in a residential zoning district or in areas bordering a
residential zoning district shall use a blower nozzle extension and shall run the blower at a low speed to
minimize noise. No more than one blower shall be operated at a residence at any time.
(Ord. No. 1997-2 § 1.)
10.80.050 REMOVAL OF DEBRIS.
No material or matter blown by leaf blowers shall be blown upon neighboring properties or onto any
portion of the public right-of-way, including but not limited to sidewalks and streets, without being
immediately removed.
(Ord. No. 1997-2 § 1.)
10.80.060 VIOLATIONS.
It is unlawful for any person or entity to violate the provisions of this chapter.
(Ord. No. 1997-2 § 1.)

10.80.070 CONSTRUCTION.
No section of this chapter shall impose a mandatory duty on the City, or on any officer, official, agent,
employee, board, council, or commission of the City. Instead, if any section purports to impose a
mandatory duty of enforcement, that section shall be deemed to invest the City, and the appropriate
officer, official, agent, employee, board, council, or commission with discretion to enforce the section or
not to enforce it.
(Ord. No. 1997-2 § 1.)

PLEASE BAN GAS POWERED LEAF BLOWERS

From Eric Sweet
Date Mon 10/6/2025 7:12 AM
To City Council (San Mateo) <CityCouncil@cityofsanmateo.org>

Polluting, Noisy, and completely unnecessary!
Leaf blowers are the most obnoxious, horrible appliance in residential neighborhoods.

The gas powered ones have 2 stroke engines, which actively burn their lubricating oil ina
partial, very poor combustion process. This results in the creation and distribution of enormous
quantities of nasty pollutants that are then 'consumed' by residents, many of whom are children,
and unfortunately many of the workers that use these devices are unknowingly harming
themselves.

All leaf blowers are very loud. It seems ironic that people spend a fortune to create a beautiful
neighborhood with landscaped lawns and pretty houses, yet every day, while most of the
homeowners are away at work, the pretty street is racked with an endless series of ear-splitting
noise.

Did you know that every time a leaf blower is used it takes dust and particles that have settled
to the ground and blasts them into the air? Do you realize how much of this material is fecal
matter from pets and the many random creatures that populate our bucolic spaces? What do
you think this does to air quality? How does this make it better for the many folks that have
asthma or other respiratory conditions?

And we know that every time the blower is used, it simply spreads the detritus into the street
and then back into the neighboring yard.

Use a rake, stop the noisy, polluting blowing.

Blowers are completely unnecessary.

Thank you.

Eric Sweet
Resident and property owner in San Mateo County.

Support for Banning Gas-Powered Leaf Blowers (Agenda Item 17)

From Christian Kungler
Date Mon 10/6/2025 9:38 AM
To City Council (San Mateo) <CityCouncil@cityofsanmateo.org>

Dear Mayor and Members of the City Council,

| am a resident of San Mateo writing to express my strong support for an ordinance banning gas
powered leaf blowers.

The health and environmental impacts of these machines are well-documented. The pollution from
just one hour of using a commercial gas-powered leaf blower is equivalent to driving 1,100 miles,
according to the California Air Resources Board (Source: https://ww2.arb.ca.gov/resources/fact-
sheets/sore-small-engine-fact-sheet). As someone who grows vegetables in my yard, | am particularly
concerned about the harmful particulates they generate settling on my family's food.

Regarding the specific direction requested in the staff report for tonight's meeting, | support the
recommendations made by the Sustainability and Infrastructure Commission and urge you to:

1. Apply the hours of operation limitations to residential zones and adjacent areas only,
as the Commission recommended, to ensure safety and cleanliness in commercial districts.

2. Assign penalties for violations to the property owner, who has the ultimate responsibility for
the services they hire. This provides the clearest path for enforcement and compliance.

3. Begin enforcement nine months after the ordinance is adopted. This provides a fair and
practical transition period for both residents and landscaping businesses.

4. Continue and enhance outreach about the City's existing financial incentives to help small
businesses migrate to cleaner, electric equipment.

Thank you for your time and for your commitment to improving the quality of life and sustainability in
San Mateo. | urge you to give staff clear direction to move forward with a strong ordinance.

Sincerely,

Christian Kungler
Resident of San Mateo North Shoreview

leaves are nature’s mulch, meant to protect and build soil, insulate plant roots and shelter wildlife.

pollinators and invertebrates, soil and water quality.

In addition to these nature benefits, yard waste blown into the street can contribute to clogged storm
drains and exacerbate flooding.

Collecting and composting is definitely better than blowing into

the street, and better still, is to #L_eaveltOnTheLawn

and

#OnlyRainDownTheDrain.

Perhaps the city can emphasize the benefits of

rethinking
 garden “clean-up” as it considers its communication on the gas leaf blower ban.
Park Gardeners Trial Alternative Methods for Managing Leaf Fall
Since Parks serve many needs and purposes, there might need to be different strategies for different
parts of the park. NYC Parks Dept says, “How our horticultural staff manages leaves depends a lot on
location. In natural areas, leaves can be mostly left in place to enrich soil and control erosion. On lawns,
leaves can be mulched in place with a mulching mower, making it easier for the lawn’s soil microbes to
break down the leaves and recycle the organic matter. And in gardens, Parks gardeners carefully assess
the conditions of each space, including the other plants and trees that are nearby, to make sure there is
just the right amount of leaf litter to provide benefits like weed suppression, but not so many leaves that
they smother the garden’s plants.”
Thank you so much for thinking about these things! 
Best, Kristie

City of San Mateo
Gas Leaf Blower Ordinance Study Session
October 6, 2025
Ordinance Language
Include language and dates for banning other gas-powered tools
Offer the submitted model ordinance to other San Mateo County cities
Enforcement and Outreach
Maximize voluntary compliance, try to keep this off code enforcement’s desk. 
Offer recognition to HOAs or neighborhoods that adopt electric or no leaf blowing 
(see San Carlos Let the Leaves Lie pledge)
Remind property owners that they are the boss. They decide not only what work 
is done on their property, but also how it is done. 
Leverage SMUHA. It could ask HOAs to stop using gas leaf blowers in their 
common areas now, include this issue in its newsletters, make an announcement 
at meetings, etc. 
Use the grace period to accept complaints and issue courtesy reminders. 
Reduce friction for property owners adopting electric or no leaf blowing
Show property owners how leaf blowing is not in a property owner’s interest 
(strips and desiccates soil, etc. See https://gardzenonline.com/blogs/gardzen/
leaf-blowers-damage-soil-so-do-this-instead.
Suggest alternatives such as using leaf blower only on hard surfaces, leaving 
leaves around bushes, mulching, etc both serve plant health and make the 
electric transition easier and it costs nothing. 
Offer directory of electric or no leaf blowing services and/or list of San Mateo 
businesses that used the electric leaf blower rebate program
Suggest ways property owners can ease the transition - allow battery charging 
while their landscaper works, paying in advance, buying their own electric leaf 
blower for landscaper to use, etc. 
384 of 405

--- page 385 ---
Enforcement
Keep it Simple
One set of rules for everyone, no exemptions
Hours of operation - commercial areas. Hours of operation should apply citywide. 
The SIC argues that allowing early morning leaf blower operation is a safety concern for 
workers and if you live downtown, you’re accepting it will be noisy. The first point is 
speculative, the second is nonsense. Living downtown does not mean accepting 
unlimited noise at any hour.
Enforcement with fines to start July 1, 2026. Issue courtesy notices to both businesses 
and property owners immediately on approval of the ordinance.
Responsible party - property owners. SIC recommended the option to cite property 
owners. Quiet Clean San Mateo recommends property owner held responsible first 
because they control how the work is done. Keep things simple and clear! Property 
owner primary responsible party, business secondary, with only one party cited. 
Identifying a landscaping business can be tricky, since some do not display their 
business name.  Property owners are already held responsible for what happens on 
their property in San Mateo municipal code. See, for example, 7.16.040 PROPERTY 
NUISANCES (j) Clothes hanging in any visible portion of a front yard. & (k) Waste 
containers stored within public view or placed for collection along a street, roadway, or 
alley outside of the time limitations…If we hold property owners responsible for those 
things, surely we can hold them responsible for their contractor using hazardous tools 
on their property. We would not allow a property owner to blame a housekeeper for 
leaving clothes or trash bins out. We would likewise not allow them to avoid 
responsibility for a contractor they hired operating hazardous, prohibited equipment on 
their property. 
Questions
These are our questions to the city council and city staff. 
How exactly will Code Enforcement handle complaints? 
Requiring CE to witness violations would be very problematic. 
We don’t want multiple complaints about the same property landing on enforcement’s 
desk with no clear way to resolve the issue. Neither do we want the one or two rare 
cases of someone blatantly violating the ordinance and ignoring complaints to ruin 
things for everyone else. No one will be happy, and we will not reach our goal. 
 
Citizen affidavits work. Can look at/discuss evidence standards and so forth.
385 of 405

--- page 386 ---
May we ask code enforcement what works for them? 
What are, say, three things we could do to make their workflow function better/more 
efficiently? Some ideas: Can we deprioritize nuisance complaints to better focus on 
public safety matters, such as leaf blower violations? Could we switch other complaints 
to citizen affidavits, so code enforcement does not have to travel as much? Can we use 
a City of San Mateo phone app for reporting violations or otherwise automate receiving 
and resolving complaints? 
How can we send a positive message to property owners be about this 
ordinance? Make switching to either no leaf blowing or electric leaf blowing 
something they want to do? 
What is the oversight on contractors doing maintenance work? Is the work 
necessary? Are they using leaf blowers when better tools exist? 
What other leaf blowing can we eliminate from city operations? 
What will happen if a business found violating the ordinance does not have a San 
Mateo business license? 
Should we modify the Construction chapter of the municipal code to specify that 
landscaping services are NOT exempt from the noise ordinance? This chapter is 
very broadly written and difficult to interpret. Clarifying the Construction chapter 
could help leaf blower enforcement. 
What are some other organizations we could reach out to help the City spread the 
word and help people making the switch to electric? 
386 of 405

--- page 387 ---
Carl Weinberg, District 20 of Stamford Board of Representatives, published his leaf 
blower ordinance research on Reddit (https://www.reddit.com/r/StamfordCT/comments/
1n9zrby/leaf blower ordinances in other cities what is/)
LEAF BLOWER ORDINANCES IN OTHER CITIES: WHAT IS THE TRACK RECORD?
Hi it’s Carl Weinberg from District 20 on the Stamford Board of Representatives. I’ve 
been reading forecasts about what will happen if the BoR passes the proposed 
restrictions on gasoline-powered leaf blowers. But since well over 100 municipalities 
have already implemented similar legislation – for example, Washington DC; 
Montgomery County MD; Evanston IL; Palo Alto CA; White Plains NY; Larchmont NY; 
Cambridge MA; Montclair NJ; Maplewood NJ; etc. – we don’t have to guess what will 
happen. We can find out from them.
As part of the research I conducted as a sponsor of this ordinance, I interviewed mayors 
and city officials whose cities and towns have implemented similar ordinances. Every 
mayor and city official I interviewed praised their local ordinance for reducing air and 
noise pollution and improving quality of life, while having minimal long-term impact on 
the landscaping industry and on fire safety.
Here are some of their comments, based on real-life experiences instead of dystopian 
fantasies.
• “Our ban became year-round on January 1, 2023; people are happy without the gas 
blowers. The only time we hear from residents is if they are reporting someone 
breaking the law.”
• “People can now take a walk, sit on their porches and not be bombarded by the noise. 
Pollinators are loving it because we’re seeing more bees, butterflies and even birds 
coming back. Because they can’t use gas blowers for fall cleanup, they are mulching 
more leaves into the lawn instead of blowing off the lawn first resulting in healthier lawns 
and less tonnage for the township to pick up at the curb.” 
• “People have become more aware that these machines pose a health risk to our 
citizens, as well as the environment. There has been a public education component to 
this ban. We’ve made flyers in English, Spanish and Haitian Creole and have passed 
them around the community. We are also working with our community to let them know 
that they are the "boss" of their landscaper so that customers feel as though they can 
direct their landscapers as to how to care for their property.” 
• “Reactions have been mostly positive. We received an uptick in noise/pollution 
complaints about gas powered blowers during initial implementation, but that has 
subsided.” 
387 of 405

--- page 388 ---
• “Most landscapers have no real issue - except charging of batteries. Our town has 
large parcels so it takes multiple batteries for the work. They have to charge at each 
home they visit. For example, we have two private schools and a private college in 
Town; as well as a Horse Club. All have large expanses of fields and grounds. There 
were some initial concerns about the requirements to switch to electric leaf blowers for 
such facilities. However, the concerns expressed did not materialize after adoption and 
all are in compliance without significant issue.”
• “Reaction from residents has been nearly 100% positive. We have received at most a 
handful of complaints. We received a lot of pushback at first from landscapers, but we 
now have pretty high compliance with the law. Our residents are extremely happy with 
the ban and appreciate the quiet! Other than the initial pushback from landscapers, 
there have not been any negatives.” 
I’ve always believed in learning from the experiences of others who have been in similar 
situations. In developing this ordinance, we learned from the more than one hundred 
municipalities that have implemented similar restrictions on the use of gasoline-powered 
leaf blowers. In my view, that’s the smart way to make decisions that are in the best 
interest of Stamford’s residents and businesses.
388 of 405

--- page 389 ---

Ban of Gas Leafblowers long overdue

From Nancy

| hope the time has come to ban gas leafblowers. | previously wrote several emails in 2023 on the
subject (one appears below). Hopefully, at this time the many reasons why this would be a good idea
are clearer.

| do feel one of the important reasons is a social justice issue. We are subjecting disenfranchised
workers to long hours of unnecessary noise and air pollution in return for low wages. As my mother
was an immigrant from Peru, | have some Spanish speaking skills. Last month | was walking on
Laurelwood Drive by Laurelwood Park and engaged in a conversation in Spanish with a gardener
about leafblowers. He also has clients in one of the cities that has a ban (Menlo Park or Atherton as |
recall). He said he simply raised his rates when he had to switch to electric blowers there. As one of the
letters to you in this packet points out, homeowners who use gardeners can for the most part more
than afford to absorb any cost increases. Hence, again, it is a social justice issue to me in many ways.

| support the other letters you received in your packet supporting the ban (e.g. from Dave Clark,
Rick Sakuda, and Dustin Chase). This input demonstrates how much of an issue this is to many people.

|, by the way, have been a volunteer for Sustainable San Mateo County (helping write part of their
annual report), as well as have served as a volunteer on the City of San Mateo's Human Resources
Commission years ago. (I have volunteered for many other groups as well such as POST Peninsula
Open Space Trust).

Finally, | wonder if the City may be able to draft this legislation or separate legislation which seeks to
prevent this type of issue in the future from starting or, it that is not possible, resolving it in less than
several years’ time. | know this can be tricky, but | am wondering if there is a way with noise abatement
or emissions laws and regulations to perhaps do this. We do not know what type of equipment might
be foisted upon us in the future.

Thank you,
Nancy Gogan

To: City Council (San Mateo) <CityCouncil@cityofsanmateo.org>; City Mgr

Subject: Gas power leafblower relentless noise today
 
Hi there,
I am asking for you all to support as much as possible the elimination of daily noise
pollution in our otherwise peaceful neighborhoods by gas powered leaf blowers and
any related equipment.  These items are also bad for the environment and the
workers and residents around them.
 
I was trying hard to concentrate on work at home today and a yard close by had
a leafblower going for a long time (and loud).  Since we know and get along well with
our neighbors I thought I should investigate some.  The neighbor did not answer and
I believe was not home.  The gardener had on headphones and I could not get his
attention from outside fence for an additional 20 minutes while he slowly blew just
one small section of yard.  (Our lots are standard size.)  When I was able to get his
attention we had discussion and he said this was his allotted time.  I mentioned that
some of the other neighbors have gardeners who are much quicker with any loud
machines.  After we spoke, sure enough. he apparently was done for the day
blowing that particular yard.  I think some of the gardeners know how annoying
these machines are to many and also it is their gardening business (company) so
they have incentives to be quick.  Others, I suspect, like the young one I just spoke
with, are employed by others and have incentive to take longer blowing leaves over
the same areas for long periods of time so they can justify their employment hours
(?).  Regardless, I look forward to when these disturbing and polluting machines are
all banned.
 
Thank you for your consideration and efforts,
Nancy Gogan

Dear Mayor Newsom and Honorable City Councilmembers,

I have been advocating for a ban of gas powered leaf blowers for the past few years and have reached out to many of
you on the council.

I don’t need to reference the well documented adverse effects on the environment from short term use of these gas
powered leaf blowers, but would rather focus on the legislative power instituted by AB1346 from the state of
California to ban the sale of these machines in 2024, along with the ban instituted by the City of Burlingame last
year and the most recent ban instituted by the City of Millbrae just a few months ago. It would send a strong message
to the gardeners and landscaping companies if the City of San Mateo would join these other municipalities with a
ban on gas leaf blowers which may lead to other cities such as Belmont and San Carlos to consider bans as well.

I appreciate your consideration of a ban on gas leaf blowers which would be a benefit to the community and go along
way to protect the health and safety of its residents.

Thank you for your attention.

Best Regards,

Adam Matye

On Tue, Oct 7, 2025 at 2:22 PM Mark Miller <
> wrote:
Dear Mayor Newsom, San Mateo City Council and San Mateo City Clerk,
Thank you for taking the time to review my letter regarding the consideration of a gas leaf
blower ban for the City of San Mateo. I appreciate your ongoing commitment to protecting
both the health and well-being of our residents and our environment.
I understand that there are a variety of factors to consider when implementing a new policy,
especially regarding the operational hours for electric leaf blowers in residential areas.
However, after careful thought, I would like to address one specific concern that has been
raised regarding expanding the operational hours to include Sundays which was discussed at
the City Council Regular Meeting on Monday, October 6, 2025.
I strongly believe that adding Sunday to the operational hours would create an unnecessary
disturbance to the quiet, peaceful environment that is so vital for the well-being of San
Mateo’s residents. Sundays, in particular, serve as an important day for relaxation,
reflection, and family time. It is a day when many of us are home and deserve the
opportunity to enjoy a quieter, more serene environment.
Even the noise generated by electric powered leaf blowers can be disruptive and detrimental
to the quality of life for residents, many of whom work long hours during the week.
Limiting their use to Monday - Saturday would strike a better balance -- allowing the
necessary yard work to be done while also respecting the need for a peaceful environment.
I respectfully urge the Council to maintain the current proposal, which restricts leaf blower
use to Monday - Saturday for residential areas, and to avoid expanding the operational
hours to include Sundays. This compromise would achieve the desired environmental
393 of 405

--- page 394 ---
benefits, while also protecting the tranquility that so many of us cherish.
Once again, thank you for your leadership in protecting our environment and the health of
our community. I trust that the City Council will continue to consider both the
environmental impact and the quality of life for San Mateo residents as you move forward
with this important decision.
I appreciate your attention and your consideration of this request.
-- Mark Miller

Dear Mayor Newsom and the San Mateo City Council,
Good day. I am a resident of District 5.
I am asking the City Council to reconsider a gas leaf blower ban for the City of San
Mateo, now that the City of Burlingame has instituted its own ban effective July 1, 2024.
As we are all aware California law AB 1346 has gone into effect, however online retailers
continue to sell gas powered leaf blowers and restock their shelves given little oversight
related to enforcement, which means that this law will take several long years to have any
measurable impact on the use of these poorly regulated machines that generate a deafening
whine of noise that feels inescapable and pollute the atmosphere with high levels of
carbon dioxide.
One of the main issues that have prevented municipalities such as San Mateo to institute a
ban on gas powered leaf blowers is that landscapers are resistant to change and will have a
hard time making the switch to battery operated machines. In order to make the switch,
landscapers will need to be pushed into making the change as this group is resistant to
change until told to do so apparently.
I am asking the City Council to please have the courage and leadership needed to institute
a ban on gas powered leaf blowers to protect the environment for ourselves and more
importantly for future generations. Please consider what the City of Burlingame has
instituted and the strong message that this says to their residents and businesses, that we
care about both your health and the health of our environment with a strong ban on gas
powered leaf blowers that goes into effect in a short time table as well as restricting the
use of leaf blowers for use by certain areas one day per week and only on weekdays
thereby giving back weekends to residents to enjoy without having to endure the noise of
these machines.
I appreciate your attention and your consideration of this request.
-- Mark Miller

Background
• Other cities have implemented bans
• Burlingame, Hillsborough, Menlo Park, Palo Alto
• Previous San Mateo City Council discussion
• Focus on engagement, rebate program, and City Operations
• City Council Priority for FY 2025-26
• Develop and implement an ordinance to prohibit the use of gas leaf blowers 
within the City of San Mateo.

State and City Regulations
• State Regulations
• New equipment Model Years 2024 and later must be electric
• City Regulations – Chapter 10.80 “Operation of Leaf Blowers”
• Hours of Operation 
• Monday through Friday 8:00 am – 5:00 pm
• Saturday 9:00 – 5:00 pm
• Applicable to residential zoning districts and areas bordering 
residentially zoned neighborhoods

Hours of Operation: Should the ordinance apply electric leaf blower 
hours of operation to residential zoned and adjacent to residential zoned 
areas only or expand the electric leaf blower hours of operation to apply 
citywide?
2.
Enforcement Phasing: Should enforcement of the ordinance begin 9 
months, 12 months, or at a different time after ordinance adoption? 
3.
Assignment of penalties: Should the ordinance include the option to 
enforce penalties against the property owners and/or any other

engaged the services of a person or business utilizing gas leaf blowers?
